      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the modern state. For the historical principality, see <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Moldova_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Moldova (disambiguation)">Moldova (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "Republic of Moldova" redirects here. For the Soviet Republic, see <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>Moldova</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Moldova.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/df/En-us-Moldova.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Moldova.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <span style="font-size:85%;">sometimes </span><span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>Romanian pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Romanian" title="Help:IPA/Romanian">[molˈdova]</a></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> officially the <b>Republic of Moldova</b> (<a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>: <i lang="ro">Republica Moldova</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked" class="mw-redirect" title="Landlocked">landlocked</a> country in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> to the west and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> to the north, east, and south.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_Moldova_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_Moldova-17">[17]</a></sup> The capital city is <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Chișinău">Chișinău</a>. </p>
      <p>Most of Moldovan territory was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Moldavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Principality of Moldavia">Principality of Moldavia</a> from the 14th century until 1812, when it was <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Bucharest_(1812)" title="Treaty of Bucharest (1812)">ceded</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> (to which Moldavia was a <a href="/wiki/Vassal_state_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Vassal state of the Ottoman Empire">vassal state</a>) and became known as <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a>. In 1856, southern Bessarabia was returned to Moldavia, which three years later united with <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> to form <a href="/wiki/United_Principalities" class="mw-redirect" title="United Principalities">Romania</a>, but Russian rule was restored over the whole of the region in 1878. During the 1917 <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a>, Bessarabia briefly became an autonomous state within the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Republic" title="Russian Republic">Russian Republic</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Democratic_Republic" title="Moldavian Democratic Republic">Moldavian Democratic Republic</a>. In February 1918, the Moldavian Democratic Republic declared independence and then integrated into Romania later that year following a vote of its assembly. The decision was disputed by <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Soviet Russia</a>, which in 1924 established, within the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic">Ukrainian SSR</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian autonomous republic</a> (MASSR) on partially Moldovan-inhabited territories to the east of Bessarabia. </p>
      <p>In 1940, as a consequence of the <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact</a>, Romania was <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina" title="Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina">compelled to cede Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, leading to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> (Moldavian SSR), which included the greater part of Bessarabia and the westernmost strip of the former MASSR (east of the <a href="/wiki/Dniester_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Dniester River">Dniester River</a>). On 27 August 1991, as the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> was underway, the Moldavian SSR <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Moldovan Declaration of Independence">declared independence</a> and took the name Moldova.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Moldova" title="Constitution of Moldova">constitution of Moldova</a> was adopted in 1994. The strip of the Moldovan territory on the east bank of the Dniester has been under the <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> control of the breakaway government of <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a> since 1990. </p>
      <p>Due to a decrease in industrial and agricultural output following the dissolution of the Soviet Union, the <a href="/wiki/Service_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Service sector">service sector</a> has grown to dominate <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Moldova" title="Economy of Moldova">Moldova's economy</a> and is over 60% of the nation's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>. It is the second poorest country in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> by GDP per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Although Moldova has a relatively high <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, it is the lowest in the continent, ranking 90th in the world. </p>
      <p>Moldova is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a> with a <a href="/wiki/President_of_Moldova" title="President of Moldova">president</a> as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Moldova">prime minister</a> as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. It is a member state of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization (WTO)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe</a> (OSCE), the <a href="/wiki/GUAM_Organization_for_Democracy_and_Economic_Development" title="GUAM Organization for Democracy and Economic Development">GUAM Organization for Democracy and Economic Development</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (CIS), and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_the_Black_Sea_Economic_Cooperation" title="Organization of the Black Sea Economic Cooperation">Organization of the Black Sea Economic Cooperation</a> (BSEC). </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Moldavia_and_Moldova" title="Names of Moldavia and Moldova">Names of Moldavia and Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The name <i>Moldova</i> is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Moldova_(river)" title="Moldova (river)">Moldova River</a>; the valley of this river served as a political centre at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Founding_of_Moldavia" title="Founding of Moldavia">foundation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Principality of Moldavia</a> in 1359.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The origin of the name of the river remains unclear. According to a legend recounted by Moldavian chroniclers <a href="/wiki/Dimitrie_Cantemir" title="Dimitrie Cantemir">Dimitrie Cantemir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grigore_Ureche" title="Grigore Ureche">Grigore Ureche</a>, Prince <a href="/wiki/Drago%C8%99,_Voivode_of_Moldavia" title="Dragoș, Voivode of Moldavia">Dragoș</a> named the river after hunting an <a href="/wiki/Aurochs" title="Aurochs">aurochs</a>: following the chase, the prince's exhausted hound <i>Molda</i> drowned in the river. The dog's name, given to the river, extended to the Principality.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>For a short time in the 1990s, at the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>, the name of the current Republic of Moldova was also spelled <i>Moldava</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, the country began to use the Romanian name, <i>Moldova</i>. Officially, the name <i>Republic of Moldova</i> is designated by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Moldova" title="History of Moldova">History of Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Transnistria" title="History of Transnistria">History of Transnistria</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The prehistory of Moldova covers the period from the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">Upper Paleolithic</a> which begins with the presence of <a href="/wiki/Cro-Magnon" class="mw-redirect" title="Cro-Magnon">Homo sapiens</a> in the area of <a href="/wiki/Prehistory_of_Southeastern_Europe" title="Prehistory of Southeastern Europe">Southeastern Europe</a> some 44,000 years ago and extends into the appearance of the first written records in <a href="/wiki/Classical_Antiquity" class="mw-redirect" title="Classical Antiquity">Classical Antiquity</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greece</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2010 N.K. Anisjutkin discovered <a href="/wiki/Oldowan" title="Oldowan">Oldowan</a> flint tools at Bayraki that are 800,000–1.2 million years old.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic Stone-Age</a> era, Moldova's territory stood at the centre of the large <a href="/wiki/Cucuteni%E2%80%93Trypillia_culture" title="Cucuteni–Trypillia culture">Cucuteni–Trypillia culture</a> that stretched east beyond the <a href="/wiki/Dniester_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Dniester River">Dniester River</a> in Ukraine and west up to and beyond the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a> in Romania. The people of this civilization, which lasted roughly from 5500 to 2750 BC, practised agriculture, raised livestock, hunted, and made intricately designed pottery.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity_and_the_early_Middle_Ages">Antiquity and the early Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Antiquity and the early Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Carpian" class="mw-redirect" title="Carpian">Carpian</a> tribes inhabited Moldova's territory in the period of <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>. Between the 1st and 7th centuries AD, the south came intermittently under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> and then the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empires</a>. Due to its strategic location on a route between Asia and Europe, the territory of modern Moldova experienced many invasions in late antiquity and the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">Early Middle Ages</a>, including by <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Avars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magyars" class="mw-redirect" title="Magyars">Magyars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pechenegs" title="Pechenegs">Pechenegs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cumans" title="Cumans">Cumans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">Mongols</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mongol_and_Tatar_states_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol and Tatar states in Europe">Tatars</a>. </p>
      <p>In the 11th century, a <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a> by the name of Rodfos was possibly killed in the area by the <a href="/wiki/Blakumen" title="Blakumen">Blakumen</a> who betrayed him.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In 1164, the future <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Andronikos_I_Komnenos" title="Andronikos I Komnenos">Andronikos I Komnenos</a>, while attempting to reach the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Halych" title="Principality of Halych">Principality of Halych</a>, was taken prisoner by Vlachs, possibly in the area of future Moldova. </p>
      <p>The East Slavic <a href="/wiki/Hypatian_Chronicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypatian Chronicle">Hypatian Chronicle</a> mentions the <a href="/wiki/Bolokhoveni" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolokhoveni">Bolohoveni</a> in the 13th century. The chronicle records that this land bordered on the principalities of <a href="/wiki/Halych" title="Halych">Halych</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volhynia" title="Volhynia">Volhynia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kyiv" title="Kyiv">Kyiv</a>. Archaeological research has identified the location of 13th-century fortified settlements in this region. Alexandru V. Boldur identified Voscodavie, Voscodavti, Voloscovti, Volcovti, Volosovca and their other towns and villages between the middle course of the rivers Nistru/Dniester and Nipru/Dnieper.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> The Bolohoveni disappeared from chronicles after their defeat in 1257 by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_of_Galicia" title="Daniel of Galicia">Daniel of Galicia</a>'s troops. </p>
      <p>In the early 13th century, the <a href="/wiki/Brodnici" title="Brodnici"><i>Brodniks</i></a>, a possible <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavic</a>–<a href="/wiki/Vlachs" title="Vlachs">Vlach</a> <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassal</a> state of <a href="/wiki/Halych-Volhynia" class="mw-redirect" title="Halych-Volhynia">Halych</a>, were present in much of the region's territory (towards 1216, the Brodniks are mentioned<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (September 2019)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> as in service of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir-Suzdal" title="Vladimir-Suzdal">Suzdal</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_of_the_Principality_of_Moldavia">Founding of the Principality of Moldavia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Founding of the Principality of Moldavia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Founding_of_Moldavia" title="Founding of Moldavia">Founding of Moldavia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MoldavianPrincipalityPhysical.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c8/MoldavianPrincipalityPhysical.jpg/200px-MoldavianPrincipalityPhysical.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c8/MoldavianPrincipalityPhysical.jpg/300px-MoldavianPrincipalityPhysical.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c8/MoldavianPrincipalityPhysical.jpg/400px-MoldavianPrincipalityPhysical.jpg 2x" data-file-width="404" data-file-height="272"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MoldavianPrincipalityPhysical.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Principality of <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a> and the modern boundaries of Moldova, Ukraine, and Romania.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Founding_of_Moldavia" title="Founding of Moldavia">founding of the Principality of Moldavia</a> began with the arrival of a <a href="/wiki/Vlach" class="mw-redirect" title="Vlach">Vlach</a> <a href="/wiki/Voivode" title="Voivode">voivode</a> (military leader), <a href="/wiki/Drago%C8%99" class="mw-redirect" title="Dragoș">Dragoș</a>, soon followed by his people from <a href="/wiki/Maramure%C8%99" title="Maramureș">Maramureș</a> to the region of the <a href="/wiki/Moldova_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldova River">Moldova River</a>. Dragoș established a <a href="/wiki/Polity" title="Polity">polity</a> there as a vassal to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> in the 1350s. The independence of the <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">Principality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a> was gained when <a href="/wiki/Bogdan_I_of_Moldavia" title="Bogdan I of Moldavia">Bogdan I</a>, another Vlach voivode from Maramureș who had fallen out with the Hungarian king, crossed the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Carpathian mountains">Carpathian mountains</a> in 1359 and took control of Moldavia, wresting the region from Hungary. The Principality of <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a> was bounded by the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a> in the west, the <a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">Dniester</a> River in the east, and the Danube River and <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> to the south. Its territory comprised the present-day territory of the Republic of Moldova, the <a href="/wiki/Western_Moldavia" title="Western Moldavia">eastern eight counties</a> of Romania, and parts of the <a href="/wiki/Chernivtsi_Oblast" title="Chernivtsi Oblast">Chernivtsi Oblast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Budjak" title="Budjak">Budjak</a> region of Ukraine. Like the present-day republic and Romania's north-eastern region, it was known to the locals as <i>Moldova</i>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Between_Poland_and_Hungary">Between Poland and Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Between Poland and Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Polska_1386_-_1434.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Polska_1386_-_1434.png/200px-Polska_1386_-_1434.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Polska_1386_-_1434.png/300px-Polska_1386_-_1434.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Polska_1386_-_1434.png/400px-Polska_1386_-_1434.png 2x" data-file-width="2977" data-file-height="2929"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Polska_1386_-_1434.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Kingdom of Poland">Kingdom of Poland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a> between 1386 and 1434 showing the <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Moldavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Principality of Moldavia">Principality of Moldavia</a> as a Polish <a href="/wiki/Fief" title="Fief">fief</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The history of what is today Moldova has been intertwined with that of Poland for centuries. The Polish chronicler <a href="/wiki/Jan_D%C5%82ugosz" title="Jan Długosz">Jan Długosz</a> mentioned Moldavians (under the name <i>Wallachians</i>) as having joined a military expedition in 1342, under King <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_I_the_Elbow-high" class="mw-redirect" title="Władysław I the Elbow-high">Ladislaus I</a>, against the <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Margraviate of Brandenburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The Polish state was powerful enough to counter the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Kingdom">Hungarian Kingdom</a> which was consistently interested in bringing the area that would become Moldova into its political orbit. </p>
      <p>Ties between Poland and Moldavia expanded after the founding of the Moldavian state by <a href="/wiki/Bogdan_I_of_Moldavia" title="Bogdan I of Moldavia">Bogdan of Cuhea</a>, a Vlach <a href="/wiki/Voivode" title="Voivode">voivode</a> from <a href="/wiki/Maramure%C8%99" title="Maramureș">Maramureș</a> who had fallen out with the Hungarian king. Crossing the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Carpathian mountains">Carpathian mountains</a> in 1359, the voivode took control of Moldavia and succeeded in creating Moldavia as an independent political entity. Despite being disfavored by the brief union of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland_during_the_Piast_dynasty" title="History of Poland during the Piast dynasty">Angevin Poland</a> and Hungary (the latter was still the country's overlord), Bogdan's successor <a href="/wiki/La%C8%9Bcu_of_Moldavia" title="Lațcu of Moldavia">Lațcu</a>, the Moldavian ruler also likely allied himself with the <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>. Lațcu also accepted <a href="/wiki/Religious_conversion" title="Religious conversion">conversion</a> to <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholicism</a> around 1370, but his gesture was to remain without consequences. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Polish_influence_grows">The Polish influence grows</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The Polish influence grows">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Petru_I_of_Moldavia" title="Petru I of Moldavia">Petru I</a> profited from the end of the Polish-Hungarian union and moved the country closer to the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland_during_the_Jagiellon_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Poland during the Jagiellon dynasty">Jagiellon realm</a>, becoming a <a href="/wiki/Vassalage" class="mw-redirect" title="Vassalage">vassal</a> of king <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_II_Jagie%C5%82%C5%82o" title="Władysław II Jagiełło">Jogaila of Poland</a> on September 26, 1387. This gesture was to have unexpected consequences: Petru supplied the Polish ruler with funds needed in the war against the <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Knights" class="mw-redirect" title="Teutonic Knights">Teutonic Knights</a>, and was granted control over <a href="/wiki/Pokuttya" class="mw-redirect" title="Pokuttya">Pokuttya</a> until the debt was to be repaid; as this is not recorded to have been carried out, the region became disputed by the two states, until it was lost by Moldavia in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Obertyn" title="Battle of Obertyn">Battle of Obertyn</a> (1531). Prince Petru also expanded his rule southwards to the <a href="/wiki/Danube_Delta" title="Danube Delta">Danube Delta</a>. His brother Roman I conquered the Hungarian-ruled <a href="/wiki/Bilhorod-Dnistrovskyi" title="Bilhorod-Dnistrovskyi">Cetatea Albă</a> in 1392, giving Moldavia an outlet to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, before being toppled from the throne for supporting <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Koriatovych" title="Fyodor Koriatovych">Fyodor Koriatovych</a> in his conflict with <a href="/wiki/Vytautas_the_Great" class="mw-redirect" title="Vytautas the Great">Vytautas the Great</a> of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Lithuania</a>. Under <a href="/wiki/Stephen_I_of_Moldavia" title="Stephen I of Moldavia">Stephen I</a>, growing Polish influence was challenged by <a href="/wiki/Sigismund,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Sigismund, Holy Roman Emperor">Sigismund of Hungary</a>, whose expedition was defeated at <a href="/wiki/Ghind%C4%83oani" title="Ghindăoani">Ghindăoani</a> in 1385; however, Stephen disappeared in mysterious circumstances. </p>
      <p>Although <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Moldavia" title="Alexander I of Moldavia">Alexander I</a> was brought to the throne in 1400 by the Hungarians (with assistance from <a href="/wiki/Mircea_I_of_Wallachia" class="mw-redirect" title="Mircea I of Wallachia">Mircea I of Wallachia</a>), this ruler shifted his allegiances towards Poland (notably engaging Moldavian forces on the Polish side in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grunwald" title="Battle of Grunwald">Battle of Grunwald</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Marienburg_(1410)" title="Siege of Marienburg (1410)">Siege of Marienburg</a>), and placed his own choice of rulers in Wallachia. His reign was one of the most successful in Moldavia's history. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Ottomans_enter_the_struggle_for_control">The Ottomans enter the struggle for control</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The Ottomans enter the struggle for control">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_Cetatea_Soroca_Soroca_Fortress_(44738813601).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_Cetatea_Soroca_Soroca_Fortress_%2844738813601%29.jpg/200px-%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_Cetatea_Soroca_Soroca_Fortress_%2844738813601%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="125" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_Cetatea_Soroca_Soroca_Fortress_%2844738813601%29.jpg/300px-%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_Cetatea_Soroca_Soroca_Fortress_%2844738813601%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_Cetatea_Soroca_Soroca_Fortress_%2844738813601%29.jpg/400px-%D0%A1%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_Cetatea_Soroca_Soroca_Fortress_%2844738813601%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5690" data-file-height="3556"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:The_Soroca_fortress.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/The_Soroca_fortress.jpg/200px-The_Soroca_fortress.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/The_Soroca_fortress.jpg/300px-The_Soroca_fortress.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/The_Soroca_fortress.jpg/400px-The_Soroca_fortress.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow" style="display:flex">
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          Built during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Stephen_III_of_Moldavia" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen III of Moldavia">Stephen the Great</a> <i>(pictured above)</i>, several authors believed the <a href="/wiki/Soroca_Fort" title="Soroca Fort">Soroca Fort</a> was constructed on the site of a former <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoese</a> fortress named <i>Olhionia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>For all of his success, it was under the reign of Alexander I that the first confrontation with the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">Ottoman Turks</a> took place at Cetatea Albă in 1420. A deep crisis was to follow Alexandrel's long reign, with his successors battling each other in a succession of wars that divided the country until the murder of <a href="/wiki/Bogdan_II_of_Moldavia" title="Bogdan II of Moldavia">Bogdan II</a> and the ascension of <a href="/wiki/Peter_III_Aaron" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter III Aaron">Peter III Aaron</a> in 1451. Nevertheless, Moldavia was subject to further Hungarian interventions after that moment, as <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Corvinus" title="Matthias Corvinus">Matthias Corvinus</a> deposed Aron and backed <a href="/wiki/Alex%C4%83ndrel" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexăndrel">Alexăndrel</a> to the throne in <a href="/wiki/Suceava" title="Suceava">Suceava</a>. Petru Aron's rule also signified the beginning of Moldavia's <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> allegiance, as the ruler agreed to pay <a href="/wiki/Tribute" title="Tribute">tribute</a> to Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Mehmed II">Mehmed II</a>. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Age_of_Invasions">The Age of Invasions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: The Age of Invasions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>During this time, Moldavia was invaded repeatedly by Crimean <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a> and, beginning in the 15th century, by the Turks. In 1538, the principality became a <a href="/wiki/Tribute" title="Tribute">tributary</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, but it retained internal and partial external autonomy.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Nonetheless, the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> continued to strongly influence Moldavia both through national politics as well as on the local level through significant intermarriage between Moldavian nobility and the Polish <a href="/wiki/Szlachta" title="Szlachta">szlachta</a>. When in May 1600, <a href="/wiki/Michael_the_Brave" title="Michael the Brave">Michael the Brave</a> removed <a href="/wiki/Ieremia_Movil%C4%83" title="Ieremia Movilă">Ieremia Movilă</a> from Moldavia's throne by winning the battle of <a href="/wiki/Bac%C4%83u" title="Bacău">Bacău</a>, briefly reuniting under his rule <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, a Polish army led by <a href="/wiki/Jan_Zamoyski" title="Jan Zamoyski">Jan Zamoyski</a> drove the Wallachians from Moldavia. Zamoyski reinstalled Ieremia Movilă to the throne, who put the country under the vassalage of the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>. Moldavia finally returned to Ottoman vassalage in 1621. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transnistria">Transnistria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Transnistria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>While the region of <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_(geographical_region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Transnistria (geographical region)">Transnistria</a> was never politically part of the Principality of Moldavia, there were sizable areas which were owned by Moldavian boyars or the Moldavian rulers. The earliest surviving deeds referring to lands beyond the Dniester river date from the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed. (May 2021)">full citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Moldavian chronicle <a href="/wiki/Grigore_Ureche" title="Grigore Ureche">Grigore Ureche</a> mentions that in 1584 some Moldavian villages from beyond the Dniester in the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Kingdom of Poland">Kingdom of Poland</a> were attacked and plundered by <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossacks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2021)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many Moldavians were members of Cossacks units, with two of them, <a href="/wiki/Ioan_Potcoav%C4%83" title="Ioan Potcoavă">Ioan Potcoavă</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danylo_Apostol" title="Danylo Apostol">Dănilă Apostol</a> becoming <a href="/wiki/Hetman" title="Hetman">hetmans</a> of Ukraine. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ruxandra_Lupu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ruxandra Lupu (page does not exist)">Ruxandra Lupu</a>, the daughter of Moldavian voivode <a href="/wiki/Vasile_Lupu" title="Vasile Lupu">Vasile Lupu</a> who married <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tymish_Khmelnytsky&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tymish Khmelnytsky (page does not exist)">Tymish Khmelnytsky</a>, lived in <a href="/wiki/Ra%C8%99cov" title="Rașcov">Rașcov</a> according to Ukrainian tradition. </p>
      <p>While most of today's Moldova came into the Ottoman orbit in the 16th century, a substantial part of Transnistria remained a part of the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> until the <a href="/wiki/Second_Partition_of_Poland" title="Second Partition of Poland">Second Partition of Poland</a> in 1793. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Russian_Empire">The Russian Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The Russian Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Treaty_of_Bucharest-1812.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Treaty_of_Bucharest-1812.png/200px-Treaty_of_Bucharest-1812.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Treaty_of_Bucharest-1812.png/300px-Treaty_of_Bucharest-1812.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Treaty_of_Bucharest-1812.png/400px-Treaty_of_Bucharest-1812.png 2x" data-file-width="464" data-file-height="354"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Treaty_of_Bucharest-1812.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Territorial changes of Moldavia following the Treaty of Bucharest 1812.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Bucharest,_1812" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Bucharest, 1812">Treaty of Bucharest of 1812</a>, and despite numerous protests by Moldavian nobles on behalf of the sovereignty of their principality, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> (of which Moldavia was a <a href="/wiki/Vassal_state" title="Vassal state">vassal</a>) ceded to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> the <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">eastern half of the territory</a> of the Principality of Moldavia along with <a href="/wiki/Khotyn" title="Khotyn">Khotyn</a> and old Bessarabia (modern <a href="/wiki/Budjak" title="Budjak">Budjak</a>), which Russia had already conquered and annexed. The new Russian province was called <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia_Governorate" title="Bessarabia Governorate">Oblast of Moldavia and Bessarabia</a>, and initially enjoyed a large degree of autonomy. After 1828 this autonomy was progressively restricted and in 1871 the Oblast was transformed into the Bessarabia Governorate, in a process of <a href="/wiki/Forced_assimilation" title="Forced assimilation">state-imposed assimilation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">Russification</a>. As part of this process, the <a href="/wiki/Tsarist" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsarist">Tsarist</a> administration in Bessarabia gradually removed the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian language</a> from official and religious use.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Union_with_Romania_and_the_return_of_the_Russians">Union with Romania and the return of the Russians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Union with Romania and the return of the Russians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1856)" title="Treaty of Paris (1856)">Treaty of Paris (1856)</a> returned the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Bessarabia" title="Southern Bessarabia">southern part of Bessarabia</a> (later organised as the <a href="/wiki/Cahul_County" title="Cahul County">Cahul</a>, Bolgrad and Ismail counties) to Moldavia, which remained an autonomous principality and, in 1859, <a href="/wiki/Moldavia_and_Wallachia" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldavia and Wallachia">united</a> with <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> to form <a href="/wiki/United_Principalities" class="mw-redirect" title="United Principalities">Romania</a>. In 1878, as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Berlin_(1878)" title="Treaty of Berlin (1878)">Treaty of Berlin</a>, Romania was forced to cede the three counties back to the Russian Empire. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="A_multiethnic_colonization">A multiethnic colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: A multiethnic colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Over the 19th century, the Russian authorities encouraged the <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">colonization</a> of Bessarabia or parts of it by <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a> (Budjak), <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Moldova" title="Russians in Moldova">Russians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bessarabian_Germans" class="mw-redirect" title="Bessarabian Germans">Germans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bessarabian_Bulgarians" title="Bessarabian Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poles_in_Moldova" title="Poles in Moldova">Poles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gagauzes" class="mw-redirect" title="Gagauzes">Gagauzes</a>, primarily in the northern and southern areas vacated by Turks and <a href="/wiki/Nogais" title="Nogais">Nogai</a> <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatar</a>, the latter having been expelled in the 1770s and 1780s, during the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish Wars">Russo-Turkish Wars</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-washington_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washington-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> the inclusion of the province in the <a href="/wiki/Pale_of_Settlement" title="Pale of Settlement">Pale of Settlement</a> also allowed the immigration of more <a href="/wiki/Bessarabian_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Bessarabian Jews">Jews</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fn1_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fn1-38">[a]</a></sup> The Romanian proportion of the population decreased from an estimated 86% in 1816,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> to around 52% in 1905.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> During this time there were anti-Semitic riots, leading to an exodus of thousands of Jews to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Russian_Revolution_and_Greater_Romania">The Russian Revolution and Greater Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The Russian Revolution and Greater Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Greater_Romania.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Greater_Romania.svg/200px-Greater_Romania.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Greater_Romania.svg/300px-Greater_Romania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Greater_Romania.svg/400px-Greater_Romania.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1744" data-file-height="1270"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Greater_Romania.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Romania" title="Greater Romania">Greater Romania</a> between 1920 and 1940.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> brought in a rise in political and cultural (ethnic) awareness among the inhabitants of the region, as 300,000 Bessarabians were drafted into the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Russian Army</a> formed in 1917; within bigger units several "Moldavian Soldiers' Committees" were formed. Following the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_(1917)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Revolution (1917)">Russian Revolution of 1917</a>, a Bessarabian parliament, <a href="/wiki/Sfatul_%C8%9A%C4%83rii" title="Sfatul Țării">Sfatul Țării</a> (a National Council), was <a href="/wiki/1917_Sfatul_%C8%9A%C4%83rii_election" title="1917 Sfatul Țării election">elected in October–November 1917</a> and opened on December 3&nbsp;[<a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">O.S.</a> 21 November]&nbsp;1917. The Sfatul Țării proclaimed the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Democratic_Republic" title="Moldavian Democratic Republic">Moldavian Democratic Republic</a> (December 15&nbsp;[<a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">O.S.</a> 2 December]&nbsp;1917) within a federal Russian state, and formed a <a href="/wiki/Pantelimon_Erhan_Cabinet" title="Pantelimon Erhan Cabinet">government</a> (21 December&nbsp;[<a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">O.S.</a> 8 December]&nbsp;1917). </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_army" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian army">Romanian army</a> <a href="/wiki/Romanian_military_intervention_in_Bessarabia" title="Romanian military intervention in Bessarabia">occupied the region</a> in early January at the request of the National Council, Bessarabia proclaimed independence from Russia on February 6&nbsp;[<a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">O.S.</a> 24 January]&nbsp;1918 and requested the assistance of the French army present in Romania (general <a href="/wiki/Henri_Mathias_Berthelot" title="Henri Mathias Berthelot">Henri Berthelot</a>) and of the Romanian Army.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> On April 9&nbsp;[<a href="/wiki/Old_Style_and_New_Style_dates" title="Old Style and New Style dates">O.S.</a> 27 March]&nbsp;1918, the Sfatul Țării decided with 86 votes for, 3 against and 36 abstaining, to <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Bessarabia_with_Romania" title="Union of Bessarabia with Romania">unite with the Kingdom of Romania</a>. The union was conditional upon fulfilment of the <a href="/wiki/Land_reform_in_Romania,_1921" class="mw-redirect" title="Land reform in Romania, 1921">agrarian reform</a>, autonomy, and respect for universal human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> A part of the interim Parliament agreed to drop these conditions after <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Bukovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a> also joined the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Kingdom of Romania</a>, although historians note that they lacked the <a href="/wiki/Quorum" title="Quorum">quorum</a> to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>This union was recognized by most of the principal <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied Powers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1920)" title="Treaty of Paris (1920)">1920 Treaty of Paris</a>, which however was not ratified by all of its signatories.<sup id="cite_ref-legal_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legal-49">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/RSFSR" class="mw-redirect" title="RSFSR">newly Soviet Russia</a> did not recognize Romanian rule over Bessarabia, considering it an occupation of Russian territory.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> Uprisings against Romanian rule took place in 1919 at <a href="/wiki/Khotyn_Uprising" title="Khotyn Uprising">Khotyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bender_Uprising" title="Bender Uprising">Bender</a>, but were eventually suppressed by the Romanian Army. </p>
      <p>In May 1919, the <a href="/wiki/Bessarabian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Bessarabian Soviet Socialist Republic">Bessarabian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> was proclaimed as a government in exile. After the failure of the <a href="/wiki/Tatarbunary_Uprising" title="Tatarbunary Uprising">Tatarbunary Uprising</a> in 1924, the Moldavian Autonomous Region, created earlier in the Transnistria region, was elevated to an <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian SSR</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_and_Soviet_era">World War II and Soviet era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: World War II and Soviet era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%22Monument_to_the_villagers_who_died_in_World_War_II,_the_village_Cojusna,_Straseni_District%22_(80-ies_famous)._(6177439670).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%22Monument_to_the_villagers_who_died_in_World_War_II%2C_the_village_Cojusna%2C_Straseni_District%22_%2880-ies_famous%29._%286177439670%29.jpg/200px-%22Monument_to_the_villagers_who_died_in_World_War_II%2C_the_village_Cojusna%2C_Straseni_District%22_%2880-ies_famous%29._%286177439670%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%22Monument_to_the_villagers_who_died_in_World_War_II%2C_the_village_Cojusna%2C_Straseni_District%22_%2880-ies_famous%29._%286177439670%29.jpg/300px-%22Monument_to_the_villagers_who_died_in_World_War_II%2C_the_village_Cojusna%2C_Straseni_District%22_%2880-ies_famous%29._%286177439670%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%22Monument_to_the_villagers_who_died_in_World_War_II%2C_the_village_Cojusna%2C_Straseni_District%22_%2880-ies_famous%29._%286177439670%29.jpg/400px-%22Monument_to_the_villagers_who_died_in_World_War_II%2C_the_village_Cojusna%2C_Straseni_District%22_%2880-ies_famous%29._%286177439670%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="513"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%22Monument_to_the_villagers_who_died_in_World_War_II,_the_village_Cojusna,_Straseni_District%22_(80-ies_famous)._(6177439670).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Monument to the villagers who died in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the village <a href="/wiki/Coju%C8%99na" title="Cojușna">Cojușna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Str%C4%83%C8%99eni_District" title="Strășeni District">Strășeni District</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Annexation_by_the_USSR">Annexation by the USSR</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Annexation by the USSR">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In August 1939, the <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact</a> and its secret additional protocol were signed, by which <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> recognized Bessarabia as being within the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_sphere_of_influence" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet sphere of influence">Soviet sphere of influence</a>, which led the latter to actively revive its claim to the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Olson_1994_483_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olson_1994_483-52">[51]</a></sup> On 28 June 1940, the Soviet Union issued an <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina" title="Soviet occupation of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina">ultimatum to Romania</a> requesting the cession of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina, with which Romania complied the following day. Soon after, the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> (Moldavian SSR, MSSR) was established,<sup id="cite_ref-Olson_1994_483_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olson_1994_483-52">[51]</a></sup> comprising about 65% of Bessarabia, and 50% of the now-disbanded Moldavian ASSR (the present-day <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a>). Ethnic Germans <a href="/wiki/Heim_ins_Reich" title="Heim ins Reich">left</a> in 1940. </p> 
      <h4><span id="Reincorporation_into_Romania.2C_the_Holocaust.2C_and_the_Soviet_occupation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Reincorporation_into_Romania,_the_Holocaust,_and_the_Soviet_occupation">Reincorporation into Romania, the Holocaust, and the Soviet occupation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Reincorporation into Romania, the Holocaust, and the Soviet occupation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>As part of the 1941 <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">Axis invasion of the Soviet Union</a>, Romania regained the territories of Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina, and seized a territory which became known as <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_Governorate" title="Transnistria Governorate">Transnistria Governorate</a>. Romanian forces, working with the Germans, <a href="/wiki/Ion_Antonescu#Antonescu_and_the_Holocaust" title="Ion Antonescu">deported or massacred</a> about 300,000 Jews, including 147,000 from Bessarabia and Bukovina. Of the latter, approximately 90,000 died.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> Between 1941 and 1944 <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_resistance_during_World_War_II" title="Moldovan resistance during World War II">partisan detachments</a> acted against the Romanian administration. The Soviet Army re-captured the region in February–August 1944, and re-established the Moldavian SSR. Between the end of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Jassy%E2%80%93Kishinev_Offensive" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Jassy–Kishinev Offensive">Second Jassy–Kishinev Offensive</a> in August 1944 and the end of the war in May 1945, 256,800 inhabitants of the Moldavian SSR were drafted into the Soviet Army. 40,592 of them perished.<sup id="cite_ref-history_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-54">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360,_Bessarabien,_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg/200px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg/300px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg/400px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360%2C_Bessarabien%2C_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg 2x" data-file-width="798" data-file-height="534"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_137-065360,_Bessarabien,_Abtransport_von_Umsiedlern.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bessarabia_Germans" title="Bessarabia Germans">Bessarabia Germans</a> <a href="/wiki/Heim_ins_Reich" title="Heim ins Reich">resettling</a> after the Soviet occupation of <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a> in 1940.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the periods 1940–1941 and 1944–1953, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_deportations_from_Bessarabia_and_Northern_Bukovina" title="Soviet deportations from Bessarabia and Northern Bukovina">deportations of locals</a> to the northern <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Urals</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, and northern <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> occurred regularly, with the largest ones on 12–13 June 1941, and 5–6 July 1949, accounting from MSSR alone for 18,392<sup id="cite_ref-fn2_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fn2-55">[b]</a></sup> and 35,796 deportees respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-tismrep_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tismrep-56">[54]</a></sup> Other forms of Soviet persecution of the population included political arrests or, in 8,360 cases, execution. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Moldova_in_the_USSR_after_World_War_II">Moldova in the USSR after World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Moldova in the USSR after World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In 1946, as a result of a severe drought and excessive delivery quota obligations and requisitions imposed by the Soviet government, the southwestern part of the USSR suffered from a major <a href="/wiki/Droughts_and_famines_in_Russia_and_the_Soviet_Union" title="Droughts and famines in Russia and the Soviet Union">famine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> In 1946–1947, at least 216,000 deaths and about 350,000 cases of dystrophy were accounted by historians in the Moldavian SSR alone.<sup id="cite_ref-tismrep_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tismrep-56">[54]</a></sup> Similar events occurred in the 1930s in the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_ASSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldavian ASSR">Moldavian ASSR</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tismrep_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tismrep-56">[54]</a></sup> In 1944–53, there were several anti-Soviet resistance groups in Moldova; however the <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Ministry_for_State_Security_(USSR)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry for State Security (USSR)">MGB</a> managed to eventually arrest, execute or deport their members.<sup id="cite_ref-tismrep_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tismrep-56">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the postwar period, the Soviet government organized the immigration of working age Russian speakers (mostly Russians, <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">Belarusians</a>, and Ukrainians), into the new Soviet republic, especially into urbanized areas, partly to compensate for the demographic loss caused by the war and the emigration of 1940 and 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup> In the 1970s and 1980s, the Moldavian SSR received substantial allocations from the budget of the USSR to develop industrial and scientific facilities and housing. In 1971, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_(Soviet_Union)" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Ministers (Soviet Union)">Council of Ministers of the USSR</a> adopted a decision "About the measures for further development of the city of <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Chișinău">Kishinev</a>" (modern Chișinău), that allotted more than one <a href="/wiki/Billion" title="Billion">billion</a> <a href="/wiki/Soviet_ruble" title="Soviet ruble">Soviet rubles</a> (approximately 6.8 billion in 2018 US dollars) from the USSR budget for building projects.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Center_Balti_-_2_(1985)._(18203012941).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Center_Balti_-_2_%281985%29._%2818203012941%29.jpg/200px-Center_Balti_-_2_%281985%29._%2818203012941%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Center_Balti_-_2_%281985%29._%2818203012941%29.jpg/300px-Center_Balti_-_2_%281985%29._%2818203012941%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Center_Balti_-_2_%281985%29._%2818203012941%29.jpg/400px-Center_Balti_-_2_%281985%29._%2818203012941%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Center_Balti_-_2_(1985)._(18203012941).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/B%C4%83l%C8%9Bi" title="Bălți">Bălți</a> in <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Soviet Moldavia</a> in 1985
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Soviet government conducted a campaign to promote a Moldovan ethnic identity distinct from that of the Romanians, based on a theory developed during the existence of the <a href="/wiki/Moldavian_ASSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldavian ASSR">Moldavian ASSR</a>. Official Soviet policy asserted that the language spoken by <a href="/wiki/Moldovans" title="Moldovans">Moldovans</a> was distinct from the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian language</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Moldovenism" title="Moldovenism">Moldovenism</a>). To distinguish the two, during the Soviet period, Moldovan was written in the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Moldovan Cyrillic alphabet">Cyrillic alphabet</a>, in contrast with Romanian, which since 1860 had been written in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a>. </p>
      <p>All independent organizations were severely reprimanded, with the <a href="/wiki/National_Patriotic_Front_(Moldova)" title="National Patriotic Front (Moldova)">National Patriotic Front</a> leaders being sentenced in 1972 to long prison terms.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Commission_for_the_Study_of_the_Communist_Dictatorship_in_Moldova" title="Commission for the Study of the Communist Dictatorship in Moldova">Commission for the Study of the Communist Dictatorship in Moldova</a> is assessing the activity of the communist totalitarian regime. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Glasnost_and_Perestroika">Glasnost and Perestroika</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Glasnost and Perestroika">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In the 1980s, amid political conditions created by the <a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">glasnost</a> and <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">perestroika</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Movement_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Movement of Moldova">Democratic Movement of Moldova</a> was formed, which in 1989 became known as the nationalist <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_of_Moldova" title="Popular Front of Moldova">Popular Front of Moldova</a> (FPM).<sup id="cite_ref-lang_matei_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lang_matei-62">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> Along with several other Soviet republics, from 1988 onwards, Moldova started to move towards <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Moldova" title="Independence of Moldova">independence</a>. On 27 August 1989, the FPM organized a mass demonstration in Chișinău that became known as the <a href="/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly,_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_1989" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand National Assembly, Chișinău 1989">Grand National Assembly</a>. The assembly pressured the authorities of the Moldavian SSR to adopt a language law on 31 August 1989 that proclaimed the Moldovan language written in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a> to be the state language of the MSSR. Its identity with the Romanian language was also established.<sup id="cite_ref-lang_matei_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lang_matei-62">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lang_law_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lang_law-64">[62]</a></sup> In 1989, as opposition to the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party of Moldova">Communist Party</a> grew, there were <a href="/wiki/1989_Moldova_civil_unrest" title="1989 Moldova civil unrest">major riots in November</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_aftermath">Independence and aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Independence and aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gheorghe_Ghimpu_arboreaza_Tricolorul.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Gheorghe_Ghimpu_arboreaza_Tricolorul.jpg/170px-Gheorghe_Ghimpu_arboreaza_Tricolorul.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Gheorghe_Ghimpu_arboreaza_Tricolorul.jpg/255px-Gheorghe_Ghimpu_arboreaza_Tricolorul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Gheorghe_Ghimpu_arboreaza_Tricolorul.jpg/340px-Gheorghe_Ghimpu_arboreaza_Tricolorul.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1005" data-file-height="1311"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gheorghe_Ghimpu_arboreaza_Tricolorul.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Deputy <a href="/wiki/Gheorghe_Ghimpu" title="Gheorghe Ghimpu">Gheorghe Ghimpu</a> replaces the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet flag">Soviet flag</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova" title="Parliament of the Republic of Moldova">Parliament</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanian flag">Romanian flag</a> on 27 April 1990.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/1990_Moldovan_parliamentary_election" class="mw-redirect" title="1990 Moldovan parliamentary election">first democratic elections</a> for the local <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldovan Parliament">parliament</a> were held in February and March 1990. <a href="/wiki/Mircea_Snegur" title="Mircea Snegur">Mircea Snegur</a> was elected as <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_Moldovan_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Speaker of the Moldovan Parliament">Speaker of the Parliament</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mircea_Druc" title="Mircea Druc">Mircea Druc</a> as Prime Minister. On 23 June 1990, the Parliament adopted the Declaration of Sovereignty of the "Soviet Socialist Republic Moldova", which, among other things, stipulated the supremacy of Moldovan laws over those of the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-lang_matei_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lang_matei-62">[60]</a></sup> After the failure of the <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt">1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Declaration of Independence of Moldova">Moldova declared its independence</a> on 27 August 1991. </p>
      <p>On 21 December of the same year, Moldova, along with most of the other Soviet republics, signed the constitutive act that formed the post-Soviet <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (CIS). Moldova received official recognition on 25 December. On 26 December 1991, the Soviet Union ceased to exist. Declaring itself a <a href="/wiki/Neutral_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Neutral state">neutral state</a>, Moldova did not join the military branch of the CIS. Three months later, on 2 March 1992, the country gained formal recognition as an independent state at the United Nations. In 1994, Moldova became a member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> program, and a member of the Council of Europe on 29 June 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-lang_matei_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lang_matei-62">[60]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Transnistria_breaks_away_.281990_to_present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Transnistria_breaks_away_(1990_to_present)">Transnistria breaks away (1990 to present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transnistria breaks away (1990 to present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Pridnestrovian_Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Pridnestrovian Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Pridnestrovian Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the region east of the <a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">Dniester</a> river, <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a>, which includes a large proportion of predominantly <a href="/wiki/Russophone" class="mw-redirect" title="Russophone">russophone</a> <a href="/wiki/East_Slavs" title="East Slavs">East Slavs</a> of Ukrainian (28%) and Russian (26%) descent (altogether 54% as of 1989), an independent <a href="/wiki/Pridnestrovian_Moldavian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Pridnestrovian Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic">Pridnestrovian Moldavian Soviet Socialist Republic</a> was proclaimed on 16 August 1990, with its capital in <a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lang_matei_62-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lang_matei-62">[60]</a></sup> The motives behind this move were fear of the rise of nationalism in Moldova. In the winter of 1991–1992 clashes occurred between Transnistrian forces, <a href="/wiki/14th_Army_involvement_in_Transnistria" title="14th Army involvement in Transnistria">supported by elements of the 14th Army</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Law enforcement in Moldova">Moldovan police</a>. Between 2 March and 26 July 1992, the conflict escalated into a <a href="/wiki/War_of_Transnistria" class="mw-redirect" title="War of Transnistria">military engagement</a>. It was a brief war between Moldovan and separatist Transnistrian forces, with Russia intervening militarily on Transnistria's side. It ended with a ceasefire and the establishment of a security zone policed by a three-way peacekeeping force of Russian, Transnistrian, and Moldovan personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="Market_economy_.281992.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Market_economy_(1992)">Market economy (1992)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Market economy (1992)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>On 2 January 1992, Moldova introduced a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>, liberalizing prices, which resulted in rapid inflation. From 1992 to 2001, the country suffered a serious economic crisis, leaving most of the population below the poverty line. In 1993, the government introduced a new national currency, the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_leu" title="Moldovan leu">Moldovan leu</a>, to replace the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_cupon" title="Moldovan cupon">temporary cupon</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Moldova" title="Economy of Moldova">economy of Moldova</a> began to change in 2001; and until 2008 the country saw a steady annual growth between 5% and 10%.
