The early 2000s also saw a considerable growth of emigration of Moldovans looking for work (mostly illegally) in Russia (especially the Moscow region), Italy, Portugal, Spain, and other countries; <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a> from Moldovans abroad account for almost 38% of Moldova's <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a>, the second-highest percentage in the world, after <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> (45%).<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections:_1994-2010">Elections: 1994-2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Elections: 1994-2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/1994_Moldovan_parliamentary_election" title="1994 Moldovan parliamentary election">1994 parliamentary elections</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Agrarian_Party_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Agrarian Party of Moldova">Democratic Agrarian Party</a> gained a majority of the seats, setting a turning point in Moldovan politics. With the nationalist Popular Front now in a parliamentary minority, new measures aiming to moderate the ethnic tensions in the country could be adopted. Plans for a <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_the_unification_of_Romania_and_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Movement for the unification of Romania and Moldova">union with Romania</a> were abandoned,<sup id="cite_ref-lang_matei_62-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lang_matei-62">[60]</a></sup> and the new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Moldova_(1994)" title="Constitution of Moldova (1994)">Constitution</a> gave autonomy to the breakaway Transnistria and Gagauzia. On 23 December 1994, the Parliament of Moldova adopted a "Law on the Special Legal Status of Gagauzia", and in 1995 the latter was constituted. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chisinau_riot_2009-04-07_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Chisinau_riot_2009-04-07_02.jpg/220px-Chisinau_riot_2009-04-07_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Chisinau_riot_2009-04-07_02.jpg/330px-Chisinau_riot_2009-04-07_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Chisinau_riot_2009-04-07_02.jpg/440px-Chisinau_riot_2009-04-07_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1329"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chisinau_riot_2009-04-07_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/2009_Moldova_civil_unrest" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Moldova civil unrest">Civil unrest</a> outside the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldovan Parliament">Parliament</a> building in 2009.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After winning the <a href="/wiki/1996_Moldovan_presidential_election" title="1996 Moldovan presidential election">1996 presidential elections</a>, on 15 January 1997, <a href="/wiki/Petru_Lucinschi" title="Petru Lucinschi">Petru Lucinschi</a>, the former First Secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Communist Party of Moldova">Moldavian Communist Party</a> in 1989–91, became the country's second president (1997–2001), succeeding Mircea Snegur (1991–1996). In 2000, the Constitution was amended, transforming Moldova into a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>, with the president being chosen through <a href="/wiki/Indirect_election" title="Indirect election">indirect election</a> rather than direct popular vote. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/2001_Moldovan_parliamentary_election" title="2001 Moldovan parliamentary election">Winning 49.9% of the vote</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_Communists_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova" title="Party of Communists of the Republic of Moldova">Party of Communists of the Republic of Moldova</a> (reinstituted in 1993 after being outlawed in 1991), gained 71 of the 101 MPs, and on 4 April 2001, elected <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Voronin" title="Vladimir Voronin">Vladimir Voronin</a> as the country's third president (re-elected in 2005). The country became the first post-Soviet state where a non-reformed Communist Party returned to power.<sup id="cite_ref-lang_matei_62-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lang_matei-62">[60]</a></sup> New governments were formed by <a href="/wiki/Vasile_Tarlev" title="Vasile Tarlev">Vasile Tarlev</a> (19 April 2001 – 31 March 2008), and <a href="/wiki/Zinaida_Grecean%C3%AEi" title="Zinaida Greceanîi">Zinaida Greceanîi</a> (31 March 2008 – 14 September 2009). In 2001–2003 <a href="/wiki/Moldova%E2%80%93Russia_relations" title="Moldova–Russia relations">relations between Moldova and Russia</a> improved, but then temporarily deteriorated in 2003–2006, in the wake of the failure of the <a href="/wiki/Kozak_memorandum" title="Kozak memorandum">Kozak memorandum</a>, culminating in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Russian_ban_of_Moldovan_and_Georgian_wines" title="2006 Russian ban of Moldovan and Georgian wines">2006 wine exports crisis</a>. The Party of Communists of the Republic of Moldova managed to stay in power for eight years. The fragmentation of the liberal bloc helped consolidate its power. The decline of the Communist Party started in 2009 after Marian Lupu joined the Democratic Party.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/April_2009_Moldovan_parliamentary_election" title="April 2009 Moldovan parliamentary election">April 2009 parliamentary elections</a>, the Communist Party won 49.48% of the votes, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(Moldova)" title="Liberal Party (Moldova)">Liberal Party</a> with 13.14% of the votes, the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democratic_Party_of_Moldova" title="Liberal Democratic Party of Moldova">Liberal Democratic Party</a> with 12.43%, and the <a href="/wiki/Party_Alliance_Our_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Party Alliance Our Moldova">Alliance "Moldova Noastră"</a> with 9.77%. The controversial results of this election sparked <a href="/wiki/2009_Moldova_civil_unrest" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Moldova civil unrest">civil unrest.</a> <sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-omg.md_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-omg.md-70">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-unimedia.info_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unimedia.info-71">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:164px;max-width:164px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:162px;max-width:162px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Maia_Sandu_-_MUS2559_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Maia Sandu" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maia_Sandu_-_MUS2559_%28cropped%29.jpg/160px-Maia_Sandu_-_MUS2559_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="224" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maia_Sandu_-_MUS2559_%28cropped%29.jpg/240px-Maia_Sandu_-_MUS2559_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maia_Sandu_-_MUS2559_%28cropped%29.jpg/320px-Maia_Sandu_-_MUS2559_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1120"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Maia_Sandu" title="Maia Sandu">Maia Sandu</a>
           <br><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_Moldova" title="President of Moldova">President of Moldova</a></small>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In August 2009, four Moldovan parties (Liberal Democratic Party, Liberal Party, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Moldova" title="Democratic Party of Moldova">Democratic Party</a>, and Our Moldova Alliance) agreed to create the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_For_European_Integration" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance For European Integration">Alliance For European Integration</a> that pushed the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_Communists_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova" title="Party of Communists of the Republic of Moldova">Party of Communists of the Republic of Moldova</a> into opposition. On 28 August 2009, this coalition chose a new <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_Moldovan_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Speaker of the Moldovan Parliament">parliament speaker</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mihai_Ghimpu" title="Mihai Ghimpu">Mihai Ghimpu</a>) in a vote that was boycotted by Communist legislators. <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Voronin" title="Vladimir Voronin">Vladimir Voronin</a>, who had been <a href="/wiki/President_of_Moldova" title="President of Moldova">President of Moldova</a> since 2001, eventually resigned on 11 September 2009, but the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_presidential_election,_November%E2%80%93December_2009" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldovan presidential election, November–December 2009">Parliament failed to elect a new president</a>. The acting president Mihai Ghimpu instituted the <a href="/wiki/Commission_for_constitutional_reform_in_Moldova" title="Commission for constitutional reform in Moldova">Commission for constitutional reform in Moldova</a> to adopt a new version of the Constitution of Moldova. After the <a href="/wiki/2010_Moldovan_constitutional_referendum" title="2010 Moldovan constitutional referendum">constitutional referendum</a> aimed to approve the reform failed in September 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> the parliament was dissolved again and a <a href="/wiki/2010_Moldovan_parliamentary_election" title="2010 Moldovan parliamentary election">new parliamentary election</a> was scheduled for 28 November 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> On 30 December 2010, Marian Lupu was elected as the Speaker of the Parliament and the acting President of Republic of Moldova.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup> After the Alliance for European Integration lost a no confidence vote, the <a href="/wiki/Pro-European_Coalition" title="Pro-European Coalition">Pro-European Coalition</a> was formed on 30 May 2013. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Banking_crisis">Banking crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Banking crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In November 2014, Moldova's central bank took control of <i>Banca de Economii</i>, the country's largest lender, and two smaller institutions, <i>Banca Sociala</i> and <i>Unibank</i>. Investigations into activities at these three banks uncovered <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_bank_fraud_scandal" title="Moldovan bank fraud scandal">large-scale fraud</a> by means of fraudulent loans to business entities controlled by a Moldovan-Israeli <a href="/wiki/Business_oligarch" title="Business oligarch">business oligarch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilan_Shor" title="Ilan Shor">Ilan Shor</a>, of funds worth about 1 billion U.S. dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> The large scale of the fraud compared to the size of the Moldovan economy are cited as tilting the country's politics in favour of the pro-Russian <a href="/wiki/Party_of_Socialists_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova" title="Party of Socialists of the Republic of Moldova">Party of Socialists of the Republic of Moldova</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> In 2015, Shor was still at large, after a period of house arrest. </p> 
      <h4><span id="Pavel_Filip.27s_government_.282016.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pavel_Filip's_government_(2016)">Pavel Filip's government (2016)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Pavel Filip's government (2016)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Following a period of political instability and massive public protests, a new Government led by <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Filip" title="Pavel Filip">Pavel Filip</a> was invested in January 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_2016-02-16_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com_2016-02-16-77">[75]</a></sup> Concerns over statewide corruption, the independence of the judiciary system, and the intransparency of the banking system, were expressed. <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>'s broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Welle" title="Deutsche Welle">Deutsche Welle</a> also raised concerns over the alleged influence of Moldovan oligarch <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Plahotniuc" title="Vladimir Plahotniuc">Vladimir Plahotniuc</a> over the Filip government.<sup id="cite_ref-Romania_Curata_Deutsche_Welle_2016-02-16_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romania_Curata_Deutsche_Welle_2016-02-16-78">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/2016_Moldovan_presidential_election" title="2016 Moldovan presidential election">December 2016 presidential election</a>, Socialist, pro-Russian <a href="/wiki/Igor_Dodon" title="Igor Dodon">Igor Dodon</a> was elected as the new president of the republic. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2019_constitutional_crisis">2019 constitutional crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 2019 constitutional crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In 2019, from 7 June to 15 June, the Moldovan government went through a period of dual power in what is known as the <a href="/wiki/2019_Moldovan_constitutional_crisis" title="2019 Moldovan constitutional crisis">2019 Moldovan constitutional crisis</a>. On 7 June, the Constitutional Court, which is largely believed to be controlled by Vladimir Plahotniuc<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> from the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Moldova" title="Democratic Party of Moldova">Democratic Party</a>, announced that they have temporarily removed the sitting president, Igor Dodon, from power due to his ‘inability’ to call new parliamentary elections as the parliament did not form a coalition within 3 months of the validation of the election results. According to Moldovan constitutional law, the president may call snap elections if no government is formed after 3 months.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> However, on 8 June, the <a href="/wiki/NOW_Platform_DA_and_PAS" title="NOW Platform DA and PAS">NOW Platform DA and PAS</a> reached an agreement with the <a href="/wiki/Party_of_Socialists_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova" title="Party of Socialists of the Republic of Moldova">Socialist party</a> forming a government led by Maia Sandu as the new prime minister, pushing the Democratic Party out of power.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> This new government was also supported by Igor Dodon. The new coalition and Igor Dodon argued that the president may call snap elections after consulting the parliament but is not obligated. Additionally, because the election results were verified on 9 March, 3 months should be interpreted as 3 calendar months, not 90 days as was the case. The former prime minister, Pavel Filip from the Democratic Party, said that new parliamentary elections will be held on 6 September and refused to recognize the new coalition, calling it an illegal government. After a week of dual government meetings, some protest, and the international community mostly supporting the new government coalition, Pavel Filip stepped down as prime minister but still called for new elections.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> The Constitutional court repealed the decision on 15 June effectively ending the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="COVID-19_pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: COVID-19 pandemic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In March 2020, due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, the government called a "national red code alert" as the number of coronavirus cases in the country rose to six on 13 March 2020. Government "banned all gatherings of over 50 people until 1 April 2020 and closed all schools and kindergartens in an attempt to curb the spread of the virus". Flights were banned to Spain, Italy, France, Austria, Belgium, Czech Republic, Cyprus, Germany, Ireland, the U.K., Poland, Portugal and Romania.<sup id="cite_ref-sn1_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sn1-84">[82]</a></sup> On 17 March, Parliament declared a <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a> for at least 60 days, suspended all international flights and closed borders with neighbours Romania and Ukraine. Moldova reported 29 cases of the disease on 17 March 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-sn2_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sn2-85">[83]</a></sup> The country reported its first death from the disease on 18 March 2020, when the total number of cases reached 30.<sup id="cite_ref-atr_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atr-86">[84]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="President_Maia_Sandu_since_2020">President Maia Sandu since 2020</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: President Maia Sandu since 2020">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/2020_Moldovan_presidential_election" title="2020 Moldovan presidential election">November 2020 presidential election</a>, the pro-European opposition candidate <a href="/wiki/Maia_Sandu" title="Maia Sandu">Maia Sandu</a> was elected as the new president of the republic, defeating incumbent pro- Russia president Igor Dodon, and thus becoming the first female elected president of Moldova.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> In December 2020, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ion_Chicu" title="Ion Chicu">Ion Chicu</a>, who led a pro-Russian government since November 2019, resigned a day before the newly elected pro-Western Maia Sandu was sworn in as the new President of Moldova.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> The parliament, dominated by pro-Russian Socialists, did not accept any Prime Minister candidate, proposed by the new president.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> On 28 April 2021, Sandu dissolved the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova" title="Parliament of the Republic of Moldova">Parliament of the Republic of Moldova</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Moldova" title="Constitutional Court of Moldova">Constitutional Court</a> ruled it valid.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> Parliamentary elections <a href="/wiki/2021_Moldovan_parliamentary_election" title="2021 Moldovan parliamentary election">are scheduled to take place</a> on 11 July 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Moldova" title="Politics of Moldova">Politics of Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_Building_in_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Parliament_Building_in_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u.jpg/220px-Parliament_Building_in_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Parliament_Building_in_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u.jpg/330px-Parliament_Building_in_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Parliament_Building_in_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u.jpg/440px-Parliament_Building_in_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2775" data-file-height="1975"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_Building_in_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldovan Parliament">Moldovan Parliament</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Moldova is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative</a> democratic <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>. The 1994 Constitution of Moldova sets the framework for the government of the country. A parliamentary majority of at least two-thirds is required to amend the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Moldova" title="Constitution of Moldova">Constitution of Moldova</a>, which cannot be revised in time of war or national emergency. Amendments to the Constitution affecting the state's sovereignty, independence, or unity can only be made after a majority of voters support the proposal in a referendum. Furthermore, no revision can be made to limit the fundamental rights of people enumerated in the Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-const_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-const-92">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Presidential_palace_in_Chisinau_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Presidential_palace_in_Chisinau_01.jpg/220px-Presidential_palace_in_Chisinau_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Presidential_palace_in_Chisinau_01.jpg/330px-Presidential_palace_in_Chisinau_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Presidential_palace_in_Chisinau_01.jpg/440px-Presidential_palace_in_Chisinau_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Presidential_palace_in_Chisinau_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Presidential_Palace,_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Presidential Palace, Chișinău">Presidential Palace, Chișinău</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country's central legislative body is the <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldovan Parliament">Moldovan Parliament</a> (<i><i lang="ro" title="Romanian-language text">Parlament</i></i>), which has 101 seats, and whose members are elected by popular vote on <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">party lists</a> every four years. </p>
      <p>The head of state is the President of Moldova, who between 2001 and 2015 was elected by the Moldovan Parliament, requiring the support of three-fifths of the deputies (at least 61 votes). The president of Moldova has been elected by the parliament since 2001, a change designed to decrease executive authority in favour of the legislature. Nevertheless, the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Moldova" title="Constitutional Court of Moldova">Constitutional Court</a> ruled on 4 March 2016, that this constitutional change adopted in 2000 regarding the presidential election was unconstitutional,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> thus reverting the election method of the President to a <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">two-round system</a> <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">direct election</a>. </p>
      <p>The president appoints a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Moldova">prime minister</a> who functions as the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and who in turn assembles a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Moldova" title="Cabinet of Moldova">cabinet</a>, both subject to parliamentary approval. </p>
      <p>The 1994 constitution also establishes an <a href="/wiki/Judicial_independence" title="Judicial independence">independent</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Moldova" title="Constitutional Court of Moldova">Constitutional Court</a>, composed of six judges (two appointed by the President, two by Parliament, and two by the Supreme Council of <a href="/wiki/Magistrate" title="Magistrate">Magistrature</a>), serving six-year terms, during which they are irremovable and not subordinate to any power. The Court is invested with the power of <a href="/wiki/Judicial_review" title="Judicial review">judicial review</a> over all acts of the parliament, over presidential decrees, and over international treaties, signed by the country.<sup id="cite_ref-const_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-const-92">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_affairs">Internal affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Internal affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sediul_MAI_al_Republicii_Moldova.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Sediul_MAI_al_Republicii_Moldova.jpg/220px-Sediul_MAI_al_Republicii_Moldova.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Sediul_MAI_al_Republicii_Moldova.jpg/330px-Sediul_MAI_al_Republicii_Moldova.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Sediul_MAI_al_Republicii_Moldova.jpg/440px-Sediul_MAI_al_Republicii_Moldova.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1832"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sediul_MAI_al_Republicii_Moldova.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Internal_Affairs_(Moldova)" title="Ministry of Internal Affairs (Moldova)">Ministry of Internal Affairs (Moldova)</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 19 December 2016, Moldovan MPs approved raising the retirement age to 63 years<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> from the current level of 57 for women and 62 for men, a reform that is part of a 3-year-old assistance program agreed with the International Monetary Fund. The retirement age will be lifted gradually by a few months every year until it is fully in effect in 2028. </p>
      <p>Life expectancy in the ex-Soviet country (which is among Europe's poorest) is 67.5 years for men and 75.5 years for women. In a country with a population of 3.5 million, of which 1 million are abroad, there are more than 700,000 pensioners. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Relations_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Relations of Moldova">Foreign Relations of Moldova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moldova%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Moldova–European Union relations">Moldova–European Union relations</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:European_Union_Moldova_Locator.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/European_Union_Moldova_Locator.svg/220px-European_Union_Moldova_Locator.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/European_Union_Moldova_Locator.svg/330px-European_Union_Moldova_Locator.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/European_Union_Moldova_Locator.svg/440px-European_Union_Moldova_Locator.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="593" data-file-height="606"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:European_Union_Moldova_Locator.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Accession to the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> is a central issue in Moldovan politics
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After achieving independence from the Soviet Union, Moldova's foreign policy was designed with a view to establishing relations with other European countries, neutrality, and European Union integration. In 1995 the country was admitted to the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>. </p>
      <p>In addition to its participation in <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> programme, Moldova is also a member state of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE), the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Cooperation_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Cooperation Council">North Atlantic Cooperation Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Francophonie</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="European Bank for Reconstruction and Development">European Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a>. </p>
      <p>In 2005, <a href="/wiki/Moldova_and_the_EU" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldova and the EU">Moldova and the EU</a> established an action plan that sought to improve collaboration between its two neighbouring countries, Romania and Ukraine. At the end of 2005 EUBAM, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Border_Assistance_Mission_to_Moldova_and_Ukraine" title="European Union Border Assistance Mission to Moldova and Ukraine">European Union Border Assistance Mission to Moldova and Ukraine</a>, was established at the joint request of the presidents of Moldova and Ukraine. EUBAM assists the Moldovan and Ukrainian governments in approximating their border and customs procedures to EU standards and offers support in both countries' fight against cross-border crime. </p>
      <p>After the 1990–1992 <a href="/wiki/War_of_Transnistria" class="mw-redirect" title="War of Transnistria">War of Transnistria</a>, Moldova sought a peaceful resolution to the conflict in the Transnistria region by working with Romania, Ukraine, and Russia, calling for international mediation, and co-operating with the OSCE and UN fact-finding and observer missions. The <a href="/wiki/Foreign_minister_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign minister of Moldova">foreign minister of Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Stratan" title="Andrei Stratan">Andrei Stratan</a>, repeatedly stated that the Russian troops stationed in the breakaway region were there against the will of the Moldovan government and called on them to leave "completely and unconditionally".<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> In 2012, a <a href="/wiki/2012_Moldova_security_zone_incident" title="2012 Moldova security zone incident">security zone incident</a> resulted in the death of a civilian, raising tensions with Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_speaks_with_Russian_President_Vladimir_Putin,_Austrian_Federal_Chancellor_Christian_Kern,_and_Moldovan_President_Igor_Dodon_on_the_sidelines_of_the_St_Petersburg_International_Economic_Forum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_speaks_with_Russian_President_Vladimir_Putin%2C_Austrian_Federal_Chancellor_Christian_Kern%2C_and_Moldovan_President_Igor_Dodon_on_the_sidelines_of_the_St_Petersburg_International_Economic_Forum.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_speaks_with_Russian_President_Vladimir_Putin%2C_Austrian_Federal_Chancellor_Christian_Kern%2C_and_Moldovan_President_Igor_Dodon_on_the_sidelines_of_the_St_Petersburg_International_Economic_Forum.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_speaks_with_Russian_President_Vladimir_Putin%2C_Austrian_Federal_Chancellor_Christian_Kern%2C_and_Moldovan_President_Igor_Dodon_on_the_sidelines_of_the_St_Petersburg_International_Economic_Forum.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_speaks_with_Russian_President_Vladimir_Putin,_Austrian_Federal_Chancellor_Christian_Kern,_and_Moldovan_President_Igor_Dodon_on_the_sidelines_of_the_St_Petersburg_International_Economic_Forum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Moldovan President <a href="/wiki/Igor_Dodon" title="Igor Dodon">Igor Dodon</a> (right) with Austrian Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Christian_Kern" title="Christian Kern">Christian Kern</a> and Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, 2 June 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In September 2010, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> approved a grant of €90 million to Moldova.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> The money was to supplement US$570 million in International Monetary Fund loans,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup> World Bank and other bilateral support already granted to Moldova. In April 2010, Romania offered Moldova development aid worth of €100 million while the number of scholarships for Moldovan students doubled to 5,000.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> According to a lending agreement signed in February 2010, Poland provided US$15 million as a component of its support for Moldova in its European integration efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup> The first joint meeting of the Governments of Romania and Moldova, held in March 2012, concluded with several bilateral agreements in various fields.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> The European orientation "has been the policy of Moldova in recent years and this is the policy that must continue," <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Timofti" title="Nicolae Timofti">Nicolae Timofti</a> told lawmakers before <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_presidential_election,_2011%E2%80%932012" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldovan presidential election, 2011–2012">his election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 29 November 2013, at a summit in Vilnius, Moldova signed an <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="European Union Association Agreement">association agreement</a> with the European Union dedicated to the European Union's '<a href="/wiki/Eastern_Partnership" title="Eastern Partnership">Eastern Partnership</a>' with ex-Soviet countries.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> The ex-Romanian President <a href="/wiki/Traian_B%C4%83sescu" title="Traian Băsescu">Traian Băsescu</a> stated that Romania will make all efforts for Moldova to join the EU as soon as possible. Likewise, Traian Băsescu declared that the <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Moldova_with_Romania" class="mw-redirect" title="Unification of Moldova with Romania">unification of Moldova with Romania</a> is the next national project for Romania, as more than 75% of the population speaks Romanian.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Moldova has signed the Association Agreement with the European Union in Brussels on 27 June 2014. The signing comes after the accord has been initialed in Vilnius in November 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It can be said that religious leaders play a role in shaping foreign policy. Since the fall of the Soviet Union, the Russian Government has frequently used its connections with the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a> to block and stymie the integration of former Soviet states like Moldova into the West.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Moldova">Military of Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Moldovan_army_Capt._Deli_Ianec,_left,_role-playing_as_an_Afghan_National_Army_officer,_and_U.S._Army_Capt._Trey_Marsh,_with_Iron_Troop,_3rd_Squadron,_2nd_Cavalry_Regiment,_review_pictures_taken_after_a_search_130311-A-PU716-004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Moldovan_army_Capt._Deli_Ianec%2C_left%2C_role-playing_as_an_Afghan_National_Army_officer%2C_and_U.S._Army_Capt._Trey_Marsh%2C_with_Iron_Troop%2C_3rd_Squadron%2C_2nd_Cavalry_Regiment%2C_review_pictures_taken_after_a_search_130311-A-PU716-004.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Moldovan_army_Capt._Deli_Ianec%2C_left%2C_role-playing_as_an_Afghan_National_Army_officer%2C_and_U.S._Army_Capt._Trey_Marsh%2C_with_Iron_Troop%2C_3rd_Squadron%2C_2nd_Cavalry_Regiment%2C_review_pictures_taken_after_a_search_130311-A-PU716-004.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Moldovan_army_Capt._Deli_Ianec%2C_left%2C_role-playing_as_an_Afghan_National_Army_officer%2C_and_U.S._Army_Capt._Trey_Marsh%2C_with_Iron_Troop%2C_3rd_Squadron%2C_2nd_Cavalry_Regiment%2C_review_pictures_taken_after_a_search_130311-A-PU716-004.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Moldovan_army_Capt._Deli_Ianec,_left,_role-playing_as_an_Afghan_National_Army_officer,_and_U.S._Army_Capt._Trey_Marsh,_with_Iron_Troop,_3rd_Squadron,_2nd_Cavalry_Regiment,_review_pictures_taken_after_a_search_130311-A-PU716-004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A soldier of the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Moldova">Moldovan Army</a> at the Joint Multinational Readiness Center in <a href="/wiki/Hohenfels,_Bavaria" title="Hohenfels, Bavaria">Hohenfels</a>, Germany
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Moldovan armed forces consists of the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Ground_Forces" title="Moldovan Ground Forces">Ground Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Air_Force" title="Moldovan Air Force">Air Force</a>. Moldova has accepted all relevant arms control obligations of the former Soviet Union. On 30 October 1992, Moldova ratified the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_Conventional_Armed_Forces_in_Europe" title="Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe">Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe</a>, which establishes comprehensive limits on key categories of conventional military equipment and provides for the destruction of weapons in excess of those limits. The country acceded to the provisions of the nuclear <a href="/wiki/Non-Proliferation_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-Proliferation Treaty">Non-Proliferation Treaty</a> in October 1994 in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> It does not have nuclear, biological, chemical or radiological weapons. Moldova joined the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Treaty Organisation">North Atlantic Treaty Organisation</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> on 16 March 1994. </p>
      <p>Moldova is committed to a number of international and regional control of arms regulations such as the UN Firearms Protocol, Stability Pact Regional Implementation Plan, the UN Programme of Action (PoA) and the OSCE Documents on Stockpiles of Conventional Ammunition. </p>
      <p>Since declaring independence in 1991, Moldova has participated in UN peacekeeping missions in Liberia, Côte d'Ivoire, Sudan and Georgia. </p>
      <p>Moldova signed a military agreement with Romania to strengthen regional security. The agreement is part of Moldova's strategy to reform its military and cooperate with its neighbours.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 12 November 2014, the US donated to Moldovan Armed Forces 39 <a href="/wiki/Humvees" class="mw-redirect" title="Humvees">Humvees</a> and 10 trailers, with a value of US$700,000, to the 22nd Peacekeeping Battalion of the Moldovan National Army to "increase the capability of Moldovan peacekeeping contingents."<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Moldova" title="Human rights in Moldova">Human rights in Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>According to <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, as of 2004 "Torture and other ill-treatment in police detention remained widespread; the state failed to carry out prompt and impartial investigations and police officers sometimes evaded penalties. Political dissidents from <a href="/wiki/Ila%C8%99cu_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Ilașcu Group">Ilașcu Group</a> were released from arbitrary detention in the break-away Transdinester region only after an order of the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="European Court of Human Rights">European Court of Human Rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> In 2009, when Moldova experienced its most <a href="/wiki/2009_Moldova_civil_unrest" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 Moldova civil unrest">serious civil unrest</a> in a decade, several civilians, including <a href="/wiki/Valeriu_Boboc" class="mw-redirect" title="Valeriu Boboc">Valeriu Boboc</a>, were killed and many more injured.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to <a href="/wiki/United_States%27_Country_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices" class="mw-redirect" title="United States' Country Reports on Human Rights Practices">Human Rights Report</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">United States Department of State</a>, released in April 2011, "In contrast to the previous year, there were no reports of killings by security forces. During the year reports of government exercising undue influence over the media substantially decreased." But "Transnistrian authorities continued to harass independent media and opposition lawmakers; restrict freedom of association, movement, and religion; and discriminate against Romanian speakers."<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> Moldova "has made noteworthy progress" on religious freedom since the era of the Soviet Union, but it can still take further steps to foster diversity," said the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Rapporteur_on_Freedom_of_Religion_or_Belief" title="United Nations Special Rapporteur on Freedom of Religion or Belief">UN Special Rapporteur on freedom of religion or belief</a> <a href="/wiki/Heiner_Bielefeldt" title="Heiner Bielefeldt">Heiner Bielefeldt</a>, in Chișinău, in September 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> Moldova improved its legislation by enacting the <i>Law on Preventing and Combating Family Violence</i>, in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Moldova" title="Administrative divisions of Moldova">Administrative divisions of Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Moldova">List of cities in Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_localities_in_Moldova" title="List of localities in Moldova">List of localities in Moldova</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Moldova" title="Communes of Moldova">Communes of Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Moldova is divided into 32 districts (<i>raioane</i>, singular <i><a href="/wiki/Raion" title="Raion">raion</a></i>), three municipalities and two autonomous regions (<a href="/wiki/Gagauzia" title="Gagauzia">Gagauzia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_autonomous_territorial_unit" title="Transnistria autonomous territorial unit">Transnistria</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> The final status of Transnistria is <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Transnistria" class="mw-redirect" title="Disputed status of Transnistria">disputed</a>, as the central government does not control that territory. 10 other cities, including <a href="/wiki/Comrat" title="Comrat">Comrat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a>, the administrative seats of the two autonomous territories, also have <a href="/wiki/Municipiu" title="Municipiu">municipality status</a>. </p>
      <p>Moldova has 66 cities (towns), including 13 with municipality status, and 916 communes. Another 700 villages are too small to have a separate administration and are administratively part of either cities (41 of them) or communes (659). This makes for a total of 1,682 localities in Moldova, two of which are uninhabited.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> </p>

        </tr>

         <th rowspan="11"><br> <p><a href="/wiki/File:Riscani_panorama_02.jpg" class="image" title="Chișinău"><img alt="Chișinău" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Riscani_panorama_02.jpg/120px-Riscani_panorama_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="59" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Riscani_panorama_02.jpg/180px-Riscani_panorama_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Riscani_panorama_02.jpg/240px-Riscani_panorama_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2288" data-file-height="1130"></a><br><small><a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u" title="Chișinău">Chișinău</a></small><br> <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A2%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C,%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_16_%D1%8D%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0.jpg" class="image" title="Tiraspol"><img alt="Tiraspol" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/%D0%A2%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_16_%D1%8D%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0.jpg/120px-%D0%A2%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_16_%D1%8D%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="68" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/%D0%A2%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_16_%D1%8D%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0.jpg/180px-%D0%A2%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_16_%D1%8D%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/%D0%A2%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_16_%D1%8D%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0.jpg/240px-%D0%A2%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%BF%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%2C%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_16_%D1%8D%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B0.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2666" data-file-height="1500"></a><br><small><a href="/wiki/Tiraspol" title="Tiraspol">Tiraspol</a></small><br> </p> </th>

      <p>The largest city in Moldova is Chișinău with a population of 635,994 people. </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Moldova" title="Geography of Moldova">Geography of Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dniester_in_Moldova,_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Dniester_in_Moldova%2C_2004.jpg/220px-Dniester_in_Moldova%2C_2004.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Dniester_in_Moldova%2C_2004.jpg/330px-Dniester_in_Moldova%2C_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Dniester_in_Moldova%2C_2004.jpg/440px-Dniester_in_Moldova%2C_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="728" data-file-height="599"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dniester_in_Moldova,_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Scenery in Moldova, with <a href="/wiki/Dniester_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Dniester River">Dniester River</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dniester_near_Vadul_lui_Vod%C4%83.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Dniester_near_Vadul_lui_Vod%C4%83.jpg/220px-Dniester_near_Vadul_lui_Vod%C4%83.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Dniester_near_Vadul_lui_Vod%C4%83.jpg/330px-Dniester_near_Vadul_lui_Vod%C4%83.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Dniester_near_Vadul_lui_Vod%C4%83.jpg/440px-Dniester_near_Vadul_lui_Vod%C4%83.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dniester_near_Vadul_lui_Vod%C4%83.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Beach on the shore of <a href="/wiki/Dniester_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Dniester River">Dniester River</a> near Vadul lui Vodă
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Moldova lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/45th_parallel_north" title="45th parallel north">45°</a> and <a href="/wiki/49th_parallel_north" title="49th parallel north">49° N</a>, and mostly between meridians <a href="/wiki/26th_meridian_east" title="26th meridian east">26°</a> and <a href="/wiki/30th_meridian_east" title="30th meridian east">30° E</a> (a small area lies east of 30°). The total land area is 33,851&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (13,070&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) </p>
      <p>The largest part of the country (around 88% of the area) lies in <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a> region, between <a href="/wiki/Prut" title="Prut">Prut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dniester" title="Dniester">Dniester</a> rivers, while a narrow strip in the east is located in <a href="/wiki/Transnistria_(region)" title="Transnistria (region)">Transnistria</a> (east of the Dniester). The western border of Moldova is formed by the Prut river, which joins the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> before flowing into the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>. Moldova has access to the Danube for only about 480&nbsp;m (1,575&nbsp;ft), and <a href="/wiki/Giurgiule%C8%99ti" title="Giurgiulești">Giurgiulești</a> is the only Moldovan port on the Danube. In the east, the Dniester is the main river, flowing through the country from north to south, receiving the waters of <a href="/wiki/R%C4%83ut" title="Răut">Răut</a>, <a href="/wiki/B%C3%AEc" title="Bîc">Bîc</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ichel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ichel (page does not exist)">Ichel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botna" title="Botna">Botna</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ialpug" title="Ialpug">Ialpug</a> flows into one of the Danube <a href="/wiki/Liman_(landform)" title="Liman (landform)">limans</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Cog%C3%A2lnic" title="Cogâlnic">Cogâlnic</a> into the Black Sea chain of limans. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Orhei_Vechi,_Moldova_-_Flickr_-_Dave_Proffer_(13).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Orhei_Vechi%2C_Moldova_-_Flickr_-_Dave_Proffer_%2813%29.jpg/220px-Orhei_Vechi%2C_Moldova_-_Flickr_-_Dave_Proffer_%2813%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Orhei_Vechi%2C_Moldova_-_Flickr_-_Dave_Proffer_%2813%29.jpg/330px-Orhei_Vechi%2C_Moldova_-_Flickr_-_Dave_Proffer_%2813%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Orhei_Vechi%2C_Moldova_-_Flickr_-_Dave_Proffer_%2813%29.jpg/440px-Orhei_Vechi%2C_Moldova_-_Flickr_-_Dave_Proffer_%2813%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Orhei_Vechi,_Moldova_-_Flickr_-_Dave_Proffer_(13).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cave churches at <a href="/wiki/Old_Orhei" title="Old Orhei">Old Orhei</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Toltre_FT%C8%98T-52.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Toltre_FT%C8%98T-52.JPG/220px-Toltre_FT%C8%98T-52.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Toltre_FT%C8%98T-52.JPG/330px-Toltre_FT%C8%98T-52.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Toltre_FT%C8%98T-52.JPG/440px-Toltre_FT%C8%98T-52.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Toltre_FT%C8%98T-52.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Toltrele Prutului near <a href="/wiki/Fete%C8%99ti,_Edine%C8%9B" title="Fetești, Edineț">Fetești</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edine%C8%9B_District" title="Edineț District">Edineț District</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country is landlocked, though it is close to the Black Sea; at its closest point it is separated from the <a href="/wiki/Dniester_Liman" class="mw-redirect" title="Dniester Liman">Dniester Liman</a>, an estuary of the Black Sea, by only 3&nbsp;km of Ukrainian territory. While most of the country is hilly, elevations never exceed 430&nbsp;m (1,411&nbsp;ft) – the highest point being the <a href="/wiki/Dealul_B%C4%83l%C4%83ne%C8%99ti" class="mw-redirect" title="Dealul Bălănești">Bălănești Hill</a>. Moldova's hills are part of the Moldavian Plateau, which geologically originate from the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a>. Its subdivisions in Moldova include the Dniester Hills (Northern Moldavian Hills and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dniester-R%C4%81ut_Ridge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dniester-Rāut Ridge (page does not exist)">Dniester Ridge</a>), the Moldavian Plain (Middle Prut Valley and <a href="/wiki/B%C4%83l%C8%9Bi_Steppe" title="Bălți Steppe">Bălți Steppe</a>), and the Central Moldavian Plateau (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Ciuluc-Solone%C8%9B_Hills&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ciuluc-Soloneț Hills (page does not exist)">Ciuluc-Soloneț Hills</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Corne%C8%99ti_Hills&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cornești Hills (page does not exist)">Cornești Hills</a>—<a href="/wiki/Codri" title="Codri">Codri</a> Massive, "Codri" meaning "forests"—<a href="/w/index.php?title=Lower_Dniester_Hills&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lower Dniester Hills (page does not exist)">Lower Dniester Hills</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lower_Prut_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lower Prut Valley (page does not exist)">Lower Prut Valley</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tigheci_Hills&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tigheci Hills (page does not exist)">Tigheci Hills</a>). In the south, the country has a small flatland, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bugeac_Plain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bugeac Plain (page does not exist)">Bugeac Plain</a>. The territory of Moldova east of the river Dniester is split between parts of the <a href="/wiki/Podolian_Plateau" class="mw-redirect" title="Podolian Plateau">Podolian Plateau</a>, and parts of the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Steppe" title="Eurasian Steppe">Eurasian Steppe</a>. </p>
      <p>The country's main cities are the capital Chișinău, in the centre of the country, Tiraspol (in the eastern region of Transnistria), Bălți (in the north) and Bender (in the south-east). <a href="/wiki/Comrat" title="Comrat">Comrat</a> is the administrative centre of Gagauzia. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Moldova has a climate which is moderately continental; its proximity to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> leads to the climate being mildly cold in the autumn and winter and relatively cool in the spring and summer.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The summers are warm and long, with temperatures averaging about 20&nbsp;°C (68&nbsp;°F) and the winters are relatively mild and dry, with January temperatures averaging −4&nbsp;°C (25&nbsp;°F). Annual rainfall, which ranges from around 600&nbsp;mm (24&nbsp;in) in the north to 400&nbsp;mm (16&nbsp;in) in the south, can vary greatly; long dry spells are not unusual. The heaviest rainfall occurs in early summer and again in October; heavy showers and thunderstorms are common. Because of the irregular terrain, heavy summer rains often cause erosion and river silting. </p>
      <p>The highest temperature ever recorded in Moldova was 41.5&nbsp;°C (106.7&nbsp;°F) on 21 July 2007 in <a href="/wiki/Camenca" title="Camenca">Camenca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> The lowest temperature ever recorded was −35.5&nbsp;°C (−31.9&nbsp;°F) on 20 January 1963 in Brătușeni, Edineț county.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Moldova is split between the <a href="/wiki/East_European_Plain" title="East European Plain">East European Plain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pontic%E2%80%93Caspian_steppe" title="Pontic–Caspian steppe">Pontic–Caspian steppe</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. It is home to three terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Central_European_mixed_forests" title="Central European mixed forests">Central European mixed forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_European_forest_steppe" title="East European forest steppe">East European forest steppe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pontic_steppe" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontic steppe">Pontic steppe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-122">[120]</a></sup> Forests currently cover only 11% of Moldova, though the state is making efforts to increase their range. It had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 2.2/10, ranking it 158th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-123">[121]</a></sup> Game animals, such as <a href="/wiki/Red_deer" title="Red deer">red deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">roe deer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boar</a> can be found in these wooded areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_issues_in_Moldova_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_issues_in_Moldova-124">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The environment of Moldova suffered extreme degradation during the Soviet period, when industrial and agricultural development proceeded without regard for environmental protection.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_issues_in_Moldova_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_issues_in_Moldova-124">[122]</a></sup> Excessive use of pesticides resulted in heavily polluted topsoil, and industries lacked emission controls.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_issues_in_Moldova_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_issues_in_Moldova-124">[122]</a></sup> Founded in 1990, the <a href="/wiki/Ecological_Movement_of_Moldova" title="Ecological Movement of Moldova">Ecological Movement of Moldova</a>, a national, non-governmental, nonprofit organization which is a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">International Union for Conservation of Nature</a> has been working to restore the damage to Moldova's natural environment.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_issues_in_Moldova_124-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_issues_in_Moldova-124">[122]</a></sup> The movement is national representative of the Center "Naturopa" of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Saiga_antelope_at_the_Stepnoi_Sanctuary.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Saiga_antelope_at_the_Stepnoi_Sanctuary.jpg/220px-Saiga_antelope_at_the_Stepnoi_Sanctuary.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Saiga_antelope_at_the_Stepnoi_Sanctuary.jpg/330px-Saiga_antelope_at_the_Stepnoi_Sanctuary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Saiga_antelope_at_the_Stepnoi_Sanctuary.jpg/440px-Saiga_antelope_at_the_Stepnoi_Sanctuary.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2449" data-file-height="2076"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Saiga_antelope_at_the_Stepnoi_Sanctuary.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Noted for its vivid portrayal of the lower <a href="/wiki/Dniester_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Dniester river">Dniester river</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henryk_Sienkiewicz" title="Henryk Sienkiewicz">Henryk Sienkiewicz</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/With_Fire_and_Sword" title="With Fire and Sword">With Fire and Sword</a></i> opens with a description of <a href="/wiki/Saiga_antelope" title="Saiga antelope">saigas</a> as a way to highlight the story's exotic setting.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> Saigas are now extinct in Moldova and are a <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" class="mw-redirect" title="Critically endangered">critically endangered</a> <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Once possessing a range from the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a> through <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a> into <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and Canada's <a href="/wiki/Yukon" title="Yukon">Yukon</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saiga_antelope" title="Saiga antelope">saigas</a> survived in Moldova and Romania into the late 18th century. Deforestation, demographic pressure, as well as excessive hunting eradicated the native saiga herds which is <a href="/wiki/Critically_endangered" class="mw-redirect" title="Critically endangered">currently threatened with extinction</a>. They were considered a characteristic animal of <a href="/wiki/Scythia" title="Scythia">Scythia</a> in antiquity. Historian <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a> referred to the saigas as the <i>kolos</i>, describing it as "between the deer and ram in size" which (understandably but wrongly) was believed to drink through its nose.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Another animal which was extinct in Moldova since the 18th century until recently was the wisent. The species was reintroduced with the arrival of three European bison from <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest" title="Białowieża Forest">Białowieża Forest</a> in Poland several days before Moldova's Independence Day on August 27, 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> Moldova is currently interested in expanding their wisent population, and began talks with Belarus in 2019 regarding a bison exchange program between the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Moldova" title="Economy of Moldova">Economy of Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Moldova" title="Tourism in Moldova">Tourism in Moldova</a>
      </div>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MoldovanGDPBySector.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/MoldovanGDPBySector.svg/220px-MoldovanGDPBySector.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/MoldovanGDPBySector.svg/330px-MoldovanGDPBySector.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/MoldovanGDPBySector.svg/440px-MoldovanGDPBySector.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="1500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">

         </div>Moldova GDP by sector
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the breakup from the USSR in 1991, energy shortages, political uncertainty, trade obstacles and weak administrative capacity contributed to the decline of economy. As a part of an ambitious economic liberalization effort, Moldova introduced a convertible currency, liberalized all prices, stopped issuing preferential credits to state enterprises, backed steady land privatization, removed export controls, and liberalized interest rates. The government entered into agreements with the World Bank and the International Monetary Fund to promote growth. The economy subsequently declined from 1991 to 1999. Since 2000 the GDP (PPP) has had a steady growth as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_Moldova_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_Moldova-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>2005</th> 
         <th>2006</th> 
         <th>2007</th> 
         <th>2008</th> 
         <th>2009</th>

         <th>2012</th> 
         <th>2013</th> 
         <th>2014</th> 
         <th>2015 </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>8.41%</td> 
         <td>9.07%</td>

         <td>10.13%</td>

         <td>6.80%</td>

         <td>8.90%</td> 
         <td>1.80%</td> 
         <td>−1.10% </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Although estimates point to possible modest overvaluation of the real exchange rate, external competitiveness appears broadly adequate as reflected in strong sustained export performance.<sup id="cite_ref-imf.org_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf.org-132">[130]</a></sup> However, the near-term economic outlook is weak. Main risks to the near-term outlook relate to serious vulnerabilities and governance issues in the banking sector, policy slippages in the run up to the elections, intensification of geopolitical tensions in the region, and a further slowdown in activity in main trading partners. </p>
      <p>Moldova remains highly vulnerable to fluctuations in remittances from workers abroad (24 percent of GDP), exports to the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (CIS) and <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) (88 per cent of total exports), and donor support (about 10 per cent of government spending). The main transmission channels through which adverse exogenous shocks could impact the Moldovan economy are remittances (also due to potentially returning migrants), external trade, and capital flows. </p>
      <p>Moldova largely achieved the main objectives of the combined ECF/EFF (IMF financial credit) supported program. The economy recovered from the drought-related contraction in 2012. </p>

        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1998</td> 
         <td><span style="color:#e0584e">-6,5%</span></td> 
         <td>2008</td> 
         <td><span style="color:#090">+7,8%</span></td> 
         <td></td> 
         <td> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1999</td> 
         <td><span style="color:#e0584e">-3,4%</span></td>

         <td><span style="color:#e0584e">-6,5% </span></td>

         <td> </td>
