         <td>2000</td> 
         <td><span style="color:#090">+2,1% </span></td> 
         <td>2010</td> 
         <td><span style="color:#090">+6,9%</span></td> 
         <td></td> 
         <td> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td colspan="6">Note:<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jurnal.md/ro/economic/2016/3/15/economia-republicii-moldova-in-scadere-in-2015-ultimele-cifre-de-la-statistica/_2018-09-28_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jurnal.md/ro/economic/2016/3/15/economia-republicii-moldova-in-scadere-in-2015-ultimele-cifre-de-la-statistica/_2018-09-28-137">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-adev2018-03-16_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adev2018-03-16-138">[136]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The gross average monthly salary in the Republic of Moldova has registered a steady positive growth after 1999, being 5906 lei or 298 euros in 2018. </p>
      <p>Corporate governance in the banking sector is a major concern. In line with FSAP recommendations, significant weaknesses in the legal and regulatory frameworks must be urgently addressed to ensure stability and soundness of the financial sector. Moldova has achieved a substantial degree of fiscal consolidation in recent years, but this trend is now reversing. Resisting pre-election pressures for selective spending increases and returning to the path of fiscal consolidation would reduce reliance on exceptionally high donor support. Structural fiscal reforms would help safeguard sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-imf.org_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf.org-132">[130]</a></sup> Monetary policy has been successful in maintaining inflation within the NBM's target range. The implementation of structural reforms outlined in the National Development Strategy (NDS) Moldova 2020—especially in the business environment, physical infrastructure, and human resources development areas—would help boost potential growth and reduce poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-imf.org_132-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf.org-132">[130]</a></sup> Moldova's remarkable recovery from the severe recession of 2009 was largely the result of sound macroeconomic and financial policies and structural reforms. Despite a small contraction in 2012, Moldova's economic performance was among the strongest in the region during 2010–13. Economic activity grew cumulatively by about 24 percent; consumer price inflation was brought under control; and real wages increased cumulatively by about 13 percent. This expansion was made possible by adequate macroeconomic stabilization measures and ambitious structural reforms implemented in the wake of the crisis under a Fund-supported program. In November 2013, Moldova initialed an Association Agreement with the EU which includes provisions establishing a <a href="/wiki/Deep_and_Comprehensive_Free_Trade_Area" title="Deep and Comprehensive Free Trade Area">Deep and Comprehensive Free Trade Area</a> (DCFTA). </p> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>The country </th> 
         <th>Average monthly salary (euro) 2018 </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Moldova<sup id="cite_ref-Monitorul.fisc.md/editorial/salariului-mediu-lunar-pe-economie-in-anul-2018-este-de-6150-lei.html_2018-09-28_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Monitorul.fisc.md/editorial/salariului-mediu-lunar-pe-economie-in-anul-2018-este-de-6150-lei.html_2018-09-28-139">[137]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>€298 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Romania<sup id="cite_ref-Mediafax_2018-08-07_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mediafax_2018-08-07-140">[138]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>€966 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Ukraine<sup id="cite_ref-Index.minfin.com_2018-09-28_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Index.minfin.com_2018-09-28-141">[139]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>€276 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>Russia<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>€534 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>A political crisis in early 2013 led to policy slippages in the fiscal and financial areas. The political crisis that broke out in early 2013 was resolved with the appointment of a government supported by a pro-European center-right/center coalition in May 2013. However, delays in policy implementation prevented completion of the final reviews under the ECF/EFF arrangements.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Moldova-chisineu-Mall-Dova.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Moldova-chisineu-Mall-Dova.jpg/220px-Moldova-chisineu-Mall-Dova.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Moldova-chisineu-Mall-Dova.jpg/330px-Moldova-chisineu-Mall-Dova.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Moldova-chisineu-Mall-Dova.jpg/440px-Moldova-chisineu-Mall-Dova.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1484"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Moldova-chisineu-Mall-Dova.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Malldova" title="Malldova">MallDova</a> shopping centre in Chișinău
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite a sharp decline in poverty in recent years, Moldova remains one of the poorest countries in Europe and structural reforms are needed to promote sustainable growth. Based on the Europe and Central Asia (ECA) regional poverty line of US$5/day (PPP), 55 percent of the population was poor in 2011. While this was significantly lower than 94 percent in 2002, Moldova's poverty rate is still more than double the ECA average of 25 percent. The NDS—Moldova (National Development System) 2020, which was published in November 2012, focuses on several critical areas to boost economic development and reduce poverty. These include education, infrastructure, financial sector, business climate, energy consumption, pension system, and judicial framework. Following the <a href="/wiki/1998_Russian_financial_crisis" title="1998 Russian financial crisis">regional financial crisis in 1998</a>, Moldova has made significant progress towards achieving and retaining macroeconomic and financial stabilization. It has, furthermore, implemented many structural and institutional reforms that are indispensable for the efficient functioning of a market economy. These efforts have helped maintain macroeconomic and financial stability under difficult external circumstances, enabled the resumption of economic growth and contributed to establishing an environment conducive to the economy's further growth and development in the medium term.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The government's goal of <a href="/wiki/Moldova%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Moldova–European Union relations">EU integration</a> has resulted in some market-oriented progress. Moldova experienced better than expected economic growth in 2013 due to increased agriculture production, to economic policies adopted by the Moldovan government since 2009, and to the receipt of EU trade preferences connecting Moldovan products to the world's largest market. Moldova has signed the <a href="/wiki/Moldova%E2%80%93European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="Moldova–European Union Association Agreement">Association Agreement</a> and the Deep and Comprehensive Free Trade Agreement with the European Union during summer 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> Moldova has also achieved a Free Visa Regime<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup> with the EU which represents the biggest achievement of Moldovan diplomacy since independence.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> Still, growth has been hampered by high prices for Russian natural gas, a Russian import ban on Moldovan wine, increased foreign scrutiny of Moldovan agricultural products, and by Moldova's large external debt. Over the longer term, Moldova's economy remains vulnerable to political uncertainty, weak administrative capacity, vested bureaucratic interests, corruption, higher fuel prices, Russian pressure, and the separatist regime in Moldova's Transnistria region.<sup id="cite_ref-indexmundi.com_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indexmundi.com-146">[144]</a></sup> According to IMF World Economic Outlook April 2014, the Moldovan GDP (PPP) per capita is 3,927 International Dollars,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> excluding grey economy and tax evasion. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Moldova" title="Energy in Moldova">Energy in Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>With few natural energy resources, Moldova imports almost all of its energy supplies from Russia and Ukraine. Moldova's dependence on Russian energy is underscored by a growing US$5 billion debt to Russian natural gas supplier Gazprom, largely the result of unreimbursed natural gas consumption in the separatist Transnistria region. In August 2013, work began on a new pipeline between Moldova and Romania that may eventually break Russia's monopoly on Moldova's gas supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-indexmundi.com_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indexmundi.com-146">[144]</a></sup> Moldova is a partner country of the EU <a href="/wiki/INOGATE" title="INOGATE">INOGATE</a> energy programme, which has four key topics: enhancing <a href="/wiki/Energy_security" title="Energy security">energy security</a>, <a href="/wiki/Technological_convergence" title="Technological convergence">convergence</a> of member state <a href="/wiki/Energy_market" title="Energy market">energy markets</a> on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Internal_energy_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal energy market">EU internal energy market</a> principles, supporting <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable energy</a> development, and attracting investment for energy projects of common and regional interest.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wine_industry">Wine industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Wine industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_wine" title="Moldovan wine">Moldovan wine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mile%C5%9Ftii_Mici_(3944427747).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mile%C5%9Ftii_Mici_%283944427747%29.jpg/220px-Mile%C5%9Ftii_Mici_%283944427747%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mile%C5%9Ftii_Mici_%283944427747%29.jpg/330px-Mile%C5%9Ftii_Mici_%283944427747%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Mile%C5%9Ftii_Mici_%283944427747%29.jpg/440px-Mile%C5%9Ftii_Mici_%283944427747%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mile%C5%9Ftii_Mici_(3944427747).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mile%C8%99tii_Mici" title="Mileștii Mici">Mileștii Mici</a> is home to the world's biggest <a href="/wiki/Wine_cellars" class="mw-redirect" title="Wine cellars">wine cellars</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country has a well-established <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> industry. It has a vineyard area of 147,000 hectares (360,000 acres), of which 102,500&nbsp;ha (253,000 acres) are used for commercial production. Most of the country's wine production is made for export. Many families have their own recipes and <a href="/wiki/Grape_varieties" class="mw-redirect" title="Grape varieties">grape varieties</a> that have been passed down through the generations. There are 3 historical wine regions: Valul lui Traian (south west), Stefan Voda (south east) and Codru (center), destined for the production of wines with protected geographic indication.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mile%C8%99tii_Mici_(winery)" title="Mileștii Mici (winery)">Mileștii Mici</a> is the home of the largest wine cellar in the world. It stretches for 200&nbsp;km and holds almost 2 million bottles of wine<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Moldova" title="Agriculture in Moldova">Agriculture in Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Moldova's <a href="/wiki/Chernozem" title="Chernozem">rich soil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate</a> <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a> (with warm summers and mild winters) have made the country one of the most productive agricultural regions since ancient times, and a major supplier of agricultural products in southeastern Europe. In agriculture, the economic reform started with the land cadastre reform.<sup id="cite_ref-cadastre_law_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cadastre_law-152">[150]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">Moldova's</a> agricultural products include vegetables, fruits, grapes, <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>, and grains.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Moldova" title="Transport in Moldova">Transport in Moldova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Rail transport in Moldova">Rail transport in Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chisinau_Airport_KIV.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Chisinau_Airport_KIV.jpg/220px-Chisinau_Airport_KIV.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Chisinau_Airport_KIV.jpg/330px-Chisinau_Airport_KIV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Chisinau_Airport_KIV.jpg/440px-Chisinau_Airport_KIV.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chisinau_Airport_KIV.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_International_Airport" title="Chișinău International Airport">Chișinău International Airport</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The main means of transportation in Moldova are railways 1,138&nbsp;km (707&nbsp;mi) and a highway system (12,730&nbsp;km or 7,910&nbsp;mi overall, including 10,937&nbsp;km or 6,796&nbsp;mi of paved surfaces). The sole international air gateway of Moldova is the <a href="/wiki/Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_International_Airport" title="Chișinău International Airport">Chișinău International Airport</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Giurgiule%C8%99ti" title="Giurgiulești">Giurgiulești</a> terminal on the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> is compatible with small seagoing vessels. Shipping on the lower <a href="/wiki/Prut" title="Prut">Prut</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nistru" class="mw-redirect" title="Nistru">Nistru</a> rivers plays only a modest role in the country's transportation system. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Telecommunications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Moldova" title="Telecommunications in Moldova">Telecommunications in Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The first million mobile telephone users were registered in September 2005. The number of mobile telephone users in Moldova increased by 47.3% in the first quarter of 2008 against the last year and exceeded 2.89 million.<sup id="cite_ref-2mil_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2mil-154">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2009, Moldova was the first country in the world to launch high-definition voice services (<a href="/wiki/HD_voice" class="mw-redirect" title="HD voice">HD voice</a>) for mobile phones, and the first country in Europe to launch 14.4 Mbit/s mobile broadband on a national scale, with over 40% population coverage.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there are around 1,295,000 <a href="/wiki/Internet_in_Moldova" title="Internet in Moldova">Internet users in Moldova</a> with overall Internet penetration of 35.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 6 June 2012, the Government approved the licensing of 4G / LTE for mobile operators.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Moldova" title="Demographics of Moldova">Demographics of Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_composition">Ethnic composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Ethnic composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>As of 2014 census, <a href="/wiki/Moldovans" title="Moldovans">Moldovans</a> were the largest ethnic group of Moldova (75.1% of the population). In addition, 7.0% of the population declared themselves <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a>, amid the <a href="/wiki/Controversy_over_ethnic_and_linguistic_identity_in_Moldova" title="Controversy over ethnic and linguistic identity in Moldova">controversy over ethnic and linguistic identity in Moldova</a>. Although historical, the polarization based on ethnolinguistic criteria of the majority ethnic group reappeared with the national revival movement of the late 1980s, and, so far, there is no consensus regarding the mainstream identity in the Republic of Moldova (Moldovan or Romanian).<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country has also important minority ethnic communities, as shown in the table below. <a href="/wiki/Gagauz_people_in_Moldova" title="Gagauz people in Moldova">Gagauz</a>, 4.4% of the population, are <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a> <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> people. <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_Moldova" title="Greeks in Moldova">Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Moldova" title="Armenians in Moldova">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poles_in_Moldova" title="Poles in Moldova">Poles</a>, Ukrainians, although not numerous, were present since as early as the 17th century, and had left cultural marks. The 19th century saw the arrival of many more Ukrainians from <a href="/wiki/Podolia" title="Podolia">Podolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Central_Europe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Galicia (Central Europe)">Galicia</a>, as well as new communities, such as <a href="/wiki/Lipovans" title="Lipovans">Lipovans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Moldova" title="Russians in Moldova">Russians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bessarabian_Bulgarians" title="Bessarabian Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia_Germans" title="Bessarabia Germans">Germans</a>. Most of Moldova's <a href="/wiki/Bessarabian_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Bessarabian Jews">Jewish population</a> emigrated away between 1979 and 2004. </p>

        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td colspan="13" align="center"><b>**</b> There were numerous allegations that the ethnic affiliation numbers were rigged: 7 out of 10 observer groups of the Council of Europe reported a significant number of cases where census-takers recommended respondents declare themselves Moldovans rather than Romanians. Complicating the interpretation of the results, 18.8% of respondents that identified themselves as Moldovans declared Romanian to be their native language.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Census_(2014)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldovan Census (2014)">2014 census</a> preliminary data, 2,998,235 inhabitants lived in Moldova (within the areas controlled by the central government), an 11.3% decrease from the figure recorded at the 2004 census. The <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a> rate was 45% of the total population living in urban areas (as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Etnie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Etnie.jpg/350px-Etnie.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="495" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Etnie.jpg/525px-Etnie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Etnie.jpg/700px-Etnie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1608" data-file-height="2272"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Etnie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ethnic map of the Republic of Moldova (2014)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the last census in Transnistria (October 2015), the population of the region was 475,373, a 14.47% decrease from the figure recorded at the 2004 census. The <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a> rate was 69.9%. By ethnic composition, the population of Transnistria was distributed as follows: Russians - 29.1%, Moldovans - 28.6%, Ukrainians - 22.9%, Bulgarians - 2.4%, Gagauzians - 1.1%, Belarusians - 0.5%, Transnistrian - 0.2%, other nationalities - 1.4%. About 14% of the population did not declare their nationality. Also, for the first time, the population had the option to identify as "Transnistrian".<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Moldova" title="Languages of Moldova">Languages of Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_language" title="Moldovan language">Moldovan language</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian language</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The official language of Moldova is <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance language</a> related to Italian, French, Spanish, and Portuguese.<sup id="cite_ref-MCC_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MCC-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 1991 <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Moldovan Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a> names the official language Romanian.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Moldova_(1994)" title="Constitution of Moldova (1994)">Constitution of 1994</a> stated that the national language of the Republic of Moldova was <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_language" title="Moldovan language">Moldovan</a>, and its writing is based on the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-173">[171]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2013, the Constitutional Court of Moldova ruled that the name "Romanian", as used in the Declaration of Independence to identify the official language, prevails over the name "Moldovan", given in Article 13 of the Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup> </p>

         <td align="right"><i>0.9</i> </td> 
         <td align="right">11,318 </td> 
         <td align="right">0.34 </td> 
         <td align="right">6,970 </td> 
         <td align="right">0.26 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><i>Unspecified</i> </td> 
         <td colspan="4" align="center">- </td> 
         <td align="right">193,434 </td> 
         <td align="right">6.45 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr bgcolor="#e0e0e0"> 
         <th align="left">Total </th> 
         <th colspan="2">4,335,360 </th> 
         <th colspan="2">3,383,332 </th> 
         <th colspan="2">2,998,235 </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td colspan="7" align="center">* <i>The Moldovan language</i> is the dialect (glottonym) of the <i>Romanian language</i> used in the Rep. Moldova. </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>At the <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Census_(2014)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldovan Census (2014)">2014 census</a> (which did not include data from the <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistrian region</a>), 54.7% of the population named Moldovan whereas 24.0% named Romanian as their first language in daily use. Although only 4.1% are ethnic Russians, Russian is still used as the main language by 14.5% of the total population. Around 50% of ethnic Ukrainians, 33% of Gagauz, 33% of Bulgarians, and 5.7% of Moldovans declared Russian as their daily use language. </p> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <caption>

      <p>Historically Russian was taught in schools as the first foreign language, because of the relationship with the Russian Empire and Soviet Union. In the 21st century, the primary foreign language taught in the schools is English. In 2013 more than 60% of schoolchildren took it as their first foreign language. This was followed by <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, taken by less than 50% of students. Since 1996, the Republic of Moldova has been a full member of <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>. <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> was the third-ranked choice.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">

       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Moldova" title="Religion in Moldova">Religion in Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>For the 2004 census, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christians</a>, who make up 93.3% of Moldova's population, were not required to declare the particular of the two main churches they belong to. The <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_of_Chi%C8%99in%C4%83u_and_All_Moldova" title="Metropolis of Chișinău and All Moldova">Metropolis of Chișinău and All Moldova</a>, autonomous and subordinated to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_of_Bessarabia" title="Metropolis of Bessarabia">Metropolis of Bessarabia</a>, autonomous and subordinated to the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Orthodox_Church" title="Romanian Orthodox Church">Romanian Orthodox Church</a>, both claim to be the national church of the country. More than 2.0% of the population is Protestant including a growing number of Jehovah's Witnesses, 0.9% belongs to other religions, 1.0% is non-religious, 0.4% is atheist, and 2.2% did not answer the religion question at the census. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Moldova" title="Education in Moldova">Education in Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:National_Library_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova_(7992652868).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/National_Library_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova_%287992652868%29.jpg/170px-National_Library_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova_%287992652868%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/National_Library_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova_%287992652868%29.jpg/255px-National_Library_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova_%287992652868%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/National_Library_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova_%287992652868%29.jpg/340px-National_Library_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova_%287992652868%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3872"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:National_Library_of_the_Republic_of_Moldova_(7992652868).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Moldova" title="National Library of Moldova">National Library of Moldova</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are 16 state and 15<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup> private institutions of <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a> in Moldova, with a total of 126,100 students, including 104,300 in the state institutions and 21,700 in the private ones. The number of students per 10,000 inhabitants in Moldova has been constantly growing since the collapse of the Soviet Union, reaching 217 in 2000–2001, and 351 in 2005–2006. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Moldova" title="National Library of Moldova">National Library of Moldova</a> was founded in 1832. The <a href="/wiki/Moldova_State_University" title="Moldova State University">Moldova State University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Sciences_of_Moldova" title="Academy of Sciences of Moldova">Academy of Sciences of Moldova</a>, the main scientific organizations of Moldova, were established in 1946. </p>
      <p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Romania allocates 5,000 scholarships in high schools and universities for Moldovan students.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup> Likewise, more than half of preschool children in Moldova benefit from Romania funded program to renovate and equip <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergartens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup> Almost all the population is literate: the <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> of the population aged 15 and over is estimated at 99.4% (as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Moldova" title="Crime in Moldova">Crime in Moldova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_bank_fraud_scandal" title="Moldovan bank fraud scandal">Moldovan bank fraud scandal</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a> lists widespread <a href="/wiki/Crime" title="Crime">crime</a> and underground economic activity among major issues in Moldova.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_Moldova_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_Moldova-17">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">Human trafficking</a> of Moldovan women and children to other parts of Europe is a serious problem.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2014, US$1 billion disappeared from three of Moldova's leading banks.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc18615_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc18615-185">[183]</a></sup> In two days loans worth US$1 billion were transferred in to United Kingdom and <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>-registered companies whose ultimate owners are unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc18615_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc18615-185">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup> Banks are administered by the <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Moldova" title="National Bank of Moldova">National Bank of Moldova</a>, so this loss was covered from state reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc18615_185-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc18615-185">[183]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_and_fertility">Health and fertility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Health and fertility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Health in Moldova">Health in Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (TFR) in Moldova was estimated in 2015 at 1.56 children/woman,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> which is below the replacement rate of 2.1. In 2012, the average age of women at first birth was 23.9 years, with 75.2% of births being to women under 30, and 22.4% of births being to unmarried women.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal mortality rate">maternal mortality rate</a> was 41 deaths/100,000 live births (in 2010)<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rate</a> was 12.59 deaths/1,000 live births (in 2015).<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-190">[188]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> in 2015 was estimated at 70.42 years (66.55 years male, 74.54 years female).<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-190">[188]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Public expenditure on health was 4.2% of the GDP and private expenditure on health 3.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-191">[189]</a></sup> There are about 264 physicians per 100,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-191">[189]</a></sup> Health expenditure was US$138 (PPP) per capita in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_191-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-191">[189]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since the breakup of the Soviet Union, the country has seen a decrease in spending on health care and, as a result, the <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> incidence rate in the country has grown.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-192">[190]</a></sup> According to a 2009 study, Moldova was struggling with one of the highest incidence rates of multidrug-resistant tuberculosis in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-193">[191]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The percentage of adults (aged 15–49) living with <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> was estimated in 2009 at 0.40%.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emigration">Emigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Emigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Emigration_from_Moldova" title="Emigration from Moldova">Emigration from Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Emigration is a mass phenomenon in Moldova and has a major impact on the country's <a href="/wiki/Demographics" class="mw-redirect" title="Demographics">demographics</a> and economy. The <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_Intelligence_and_Security_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Moldovan Intelligence and Security Service">Moldovan Intelligence and Security Service</a> has estimated that 600,000 to one million Moldovan citizens (almost 25% of the population) are working abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eminescu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Eminescu.jpg/170px-Eminescu.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Eminescu.jpg/255px-Eminescu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Eminescu.jpg/340px-Eminescu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1126"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eminescu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mihai_Eminescu" title="Mihai Eminescu">Mihai Eminescu</a>, the national poet of Moldova and Romania
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Moldova" title="Culture of Moldova">Culture of Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Moldova's cultural tradition has been influenced primarily by the <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_the_Romanians" title="Origin of the Romanians">Romanian origins</a> of its majority population, the roots of which go back to the 2nd century AD, the period of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> colonization in <a href="/wiki/Dacia" title="Dacia">Dacia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-196">[194]</a></sup> Located geographically at the crossroads of <a href="/wiki/Italic_peoples" title="Italic peoples">Latin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavic_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic people">Slavic</a> and other cultures, Moldova has enriched its own culture adopting and maintaining traditions of neighbouring regions and of other influential sources.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup> The largest ethnic group, which had come to identify itself widely as "Moldovan" by the 14th century, played a significant role in the shaping of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Romania#Classical_age" title="Culture of Romania">classical Romanian culture</a>. The culture has been also influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> culture, the neighbouring Magyar and Slavic populations, and later by the Ottoman Turks. A strong Western European influence in Moldovan literature and arts was prevalent in the 19th century. During the periods 1812-1917 and 1944–89, Moldovans were influenced by Russian and Soviet administrative control as well and by ethnic Russian immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-culture_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture-196">[194]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country's cultural heritage was marked by numerous churches and monasteries built by the Moldavian ruler <a href="/wiki/Stephen_the_Great" title="Stephen the Great">Stephen the Great</a> in the 15th century, by the works of the later renaissance Metropolitans <a href="/wiki/Varlaam,_Metropolitan_of_Moscow" title="Varlaam, Metropolitan of Moscow">Varlaam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dosoftei" title="Dosoftei">Dosoftei</a>, and those of scholars such as <a href="/wiki/Grigore_Ureche" title="Grigore Ureche">Grigore Ureche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miron_Costin" title="Miron Costin">Miron Costin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicolae_Milescu" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicolae Milescu">Nicolae Milescu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dimitrie_Cantemir" title="Dimitrie Cantemir">Dimitrie Cantemir</a><sup id="cite_ref-fn6_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fn6-198">[c]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ion_Neculce" title="Ion Neculce">Ion Neculce</a>. In the 19th century, Moldavians from the territories of the medieval Principality of <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>, divided into <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bukovina" title="Bukovina">Bukovina</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Western_Moldavia" title="Western Moldavia">Western Moldavia</a> (after 1859, Romania), made a significant contribution to the formation of the modern Romanian culture. Among these were many Bessarabians, such as <a href="/wiki/Alecu_Donici" title="Alecu Donici">Alexandru Donici</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexandru_H%C3%A2jdeu" title="Alexandru Hâjdeu">Alexandru Hâjdeu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bogdan_Petriceicu_Hasdeu" title="Bogdan Petriceicu Hasdeu">Bogdan Petriceicu Hasdeu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constantin_Stamati" title="Constantin Stamati">Constantin Stamati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constantin_Stamati-Ciurea" title="Constantin Stamati-Ciurea">Constantin Stamati-Ciurea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costache_Negruzzi" class="mw-redirect" title="Costache Negruzzi">Costache Negruzzi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alecu_Russo" title="Alecu Russo">Alecu Russo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constantin_Stere" title="Constantin Stere">Constantin Stere</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Mihai_Eminescu" title="Mihai Eminescu">Mihai Eminescu</a>, a late <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romantic</a> poet, and <a href="/wiki/Ion_Creang%C4%83" title="Ion Creangă">Ion Creangă</a>, a writer, are the most influential <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian language</a> artists, considered national writers both in Romania and Moldova.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[196]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Moldova" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Moldova">Media of Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Moldova" title="Television in Moldova">Television in Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Moldova" title="Cinema of Moldova">Cinema of Moldova</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Moldova" title="List of newspapers in Moldova">List of newspapers in Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In October 1939, <i><a href="/wiki/Radio_Basarabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio Basarabia">Radio Basarabia</a></i>, a local station of the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_Radio_Broadcasting_Company" title="Romanian Radio Broadcasting Company">Romanian Radio Broadcasting Company</a>, was the first radio station opened in Chișinău. Television in Moldova was <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_introduction_of_television_in_countries" title="Timeline of the introduction of television in countries">introduced in April 1958</a>, within the framework of <a href="/wiki/Soviet_television" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet television">Soviet television</a>. Through cable, Moldovan viewers can receive a large number of <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Russia" title="Television in Russia">Russian channels</a>, a few <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Romania" title="Television in Romania">Romanian channels</a>, and several <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian language</a> versions of international channels in addition to several local channels.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> One Russian and two local channels are aired.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Infotag is the state news agency. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_beverage">Food and beverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Food and beverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Moldovan_cuisine" title="Moldovan cuisine">Moldovan cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sarmalute_mamaliguta.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Sarmalute_mamaliguta.JPG/220px-Sarmalute_mamaliguta.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Sarmalute_mamaliguta.JPG/330px-Sarmalute_mamaliguta.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Sarmalute_mamaliguta.JPG/440px-Sarmalute_mamaliguta.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sarmalute_mamaliguta.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A popular Moldovan dish of stuffed cabbage rolls (<a href="/wiki/Sarmale" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarmale">sarmale</a>), accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Sauerkraut" title="Sauerkraut">sauerkraut</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%C4%83m%C4%83lig%C4%83" title="Mămăligă">mămăligă</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Moldovan cuisine is similar to neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Romanian_cuisine" title="Romanian cuisine">Romania</a>, and has been influenced by elements of <a href="/wiki/Russian_cuisine" title="Russian cuisine">Russian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_cuisine" title="Turkish cuisine">Turkish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_cuisine" title="Ukrainian cuisine">Ukrainian cuisine</a>. Main dishes include <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potatoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Potatoes">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">cabbage</a>, and a variety of <a href="/wiki/Cereals" class="mw-redirect" title="Cereals">cereals</a>. Popular alcoholic beverages are <i><a href="/wiki/Moldovan_wine#Divin" title="Moldovan wine">divin</a></i> (Moldovan <a href="/wiki/Brandy" title="Brandy">brandy</a>), <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a>, and local <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>. </p>
      <p>Traditional Moldovan dishes include <a href="/wiki/Pl%C4%83cint%C4%83" title="Plăcintă">plăcinte</a> (sweet and savoury pastries with fillings such as local cheese, cabbage, potatoes, apples, sour cherries and others), <a href="/wiki/M%C4%83m%C4%83lig%C4%83" title="Mămăligă">mămăligă</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarmale" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarmale">sarmale</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Chicken_soup" title="Chicken soup">chicken soup</a> called zeamă. </p>
      <p>Total recorded adult alcohol consumption is approximately evenly split between spirits, beer and wine. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Moldova_at_ESC_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Moldova_at_ESC_2011.jpg/220px-Moldova_at_ESC_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Moldova_at_ESC_2011.jpg/330px-Moldova_at_ESC_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Moldova_at_ESC_2011.jpg/440px-Moldova_at_ESC_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1065"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Moldova_at_ESC_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Zdob_%C8%99i_Zdub" title="Zdob și Zdub">Zdob și Zdub</a> performing at the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2011" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2011">2011 Eurovision Song Contest</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Moldova" title="Music of Moldova">Music of Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Among Moldova's most prominent composers are <a href="/wiki/Gavriil_Musicescu" title="Gavriil Musicescu">Gavriil Musicescu</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C8%98tefan_Neaga" title="Ștefan Neaga">Ștefan Neaga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eugen_Doga" title="Eugen Doga">Eugen Doga</a>. </p>
      <p>In the field of pop music, Moldova has produced the band <a href="/wiki/O-Zone" title="O-Zone">O-Zone</a>, who came to prominence in 2003, with their hit song "<a href="/wiki/Dragostea_Din_Tei" title="Dragostea Din Tei">Dragostea Din Tei</a>", which topped multiple notable single charts. Moldova has been participating in the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">Eurovision Song Contest</a> since 2005. Another popular band from Moldova is <a href="/wiki/Zdob_%C8%99i_Zdub" title="Zdob și Zdub">Zdob și Zdub</a> that represented the country in the <a href="/wiki/2005_Eurovision_Song_Contest" class="mw-redirect" title="2005 Eurovision Song Contest">2005 Eurovision Song Contest</a>, finishing 6th. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Carla%27s_Dreams_in_Feb_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Carla%27s_Dreams_in_Feb_2018.jpg/220px-Carla%27s_Dreams_in_Feb_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Carla%27s_Dreams_in_Feb_2018.jpg/330px-Carla%27s_Dreams_in_Feb_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Carla%27s_Dreams_in_Feb_2018.jpg/440px-Carla%27s_Dreams_in_Feb_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="705" data-file-height="651"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Carla%27s_Dreams_in_Feb_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Carla%27s_Dreams" title="Carla's Dreams">Carla's Dreams</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In May 2007, <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Barbu" title="Natalia Barbu">Natalia Barbu</a> represented Moldova in Helsinki at the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2007" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2007">Eurovision Song Contest 2007</a> with her entry "<a href="/wiki/Fight_(song)" title="Fight (song)">Fight</a>". Natalia squeezed into the final by a very small margin. She took 10th place with 109 points. Then <a href="/wiki/Zdob_%C8%99i_Zdub" title="Zdob și Zdub">Zdob și Zdub</a> again represented Moldova in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Eurovision_Song_Contest" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Eurovision Song Contest">2011 Eurovision Song Contest</a> finishing 12th. </p>
      <p>The band <a href="/wiki/SunStroke_Project" title="SunStroke Project">SunStroke Project</a> with <a href="/wiki/Olia_Tira" title="Olia Tira">Olia Tira</a> represented the country in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Eurovision_Song_Contest" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 Eurovision Song Contest">2010 Eurovision Song Contest</a> with their hit song "<a href="/wiki/Run_Away_(SunStroke_Project_and_Olia_Tira_song)" title="Run Away (SunStroke Project and Olia Tira song)">Run Away</a>". Their performance gained international notoriety as an <a href="/wiki/Internet_meme" title="Internet meme">internet meme</a> due to the pelvic thrusting and dancing of Sergey Stepanov, the band saxophonist. He has been fittingly dubbed "<a href="/wiki/Epic_Sax_Guy" class="mw-redirect" title="Epic Sax Guy">Epic Sax Guy</a>". SunStroke Project featured again in the 2017 Eurovision entry "Hey Mama" which got third place.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[197]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2015 a new musical project by the name of <a href="/wiki/Carla%27s_Dreams" title="Carla's Dreams">Carla's Dreams</a> has risen in popularity around Moldova. <a href="/wiki/Carla%27s_Dreams" title="Carla's Dreams">Carla's Dreams</a> reached the top charts in multiple countries in Europe with the release of their song "Sub Pielea Mea" in 2016. The song received a lot of airplay and reached number one place on the charts in Moldova as well as Russia. The group is still active and released their latest album in 2017. The theme of the musical group is "Anonymous" as they perform with painted faces, hoodies and sunglasses. The identity of the group members is still unknown. </p>
      <p>Among most prominent classical musicians in Moldova are <a href="/wiki/Maria_Bie%C8%99u" title="Maria Bieșu">Maria Bieșu</a>, one of the leading world's sopranos and the winner of the Japan International Competition; pianist <a href="/wiki/Mark_Zeltser" title="Mark Zeltser">Mark Zeltser</a>, winner of the USSR National Competition, Margueritte Long Competition in Paris and Busoni Competition in Bolzano, Italy. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays">Holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Moldova" title="Public holidays in Moldova">Public holidays in Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Zimbru_Stadium.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Zimbru_Stadium.JPG/220px-Zimbru_Stadium.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Zimbru_Stadium.JPG/330px-Zimbru_Stadium.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Zimbru_Stadium.JPG/440px-Zimbru_Stadium.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1020" data-file-height="765"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Zimbru_Stadium.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Zimbru_Stadium" title="Zimbru Stadium">Zimbru Stadium</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most retail businesses close on <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">New Year's Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Republic_of_Moldova)" class="mw-redirect" title="Independence Day (Republic of Moldova)">Independence Day</a>, but remain open on all other holidays. <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> is celebrated either on 7 January, the traditional date in <a href="/wiki/Old_Calendarists" title="Old Calendarists">Old Calendarists</a> <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Churches</a>, or on 25 December, with both dates being recognized as public holidays.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[198]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Moldova" title="Sport in Moldova">Sport in Moldova</a>
      </div> 
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/Tr%C3%AEnt%C4%83" class="mw-redirect" title="Trîntă">Trîntă</a></i> (a form of <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">wrestling</a>) is the national sport in Moldova. <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is the most popular team sport. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby union</a> is popular as well. More than 10,000 supporters turn out for home internationals. Since 2004, playing numbers at all levels have more than doubled to 3,200. Despite the hardships and deprivations the national team are ranked 34th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[199]</a></sup> The most prestigious <a href="/wiki/Cycling_race" class="mw-redirect" title="Cycling race">cycling race</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Moldova_President%27s_Cup" title="Moldova President's Cup">Moldova President's Cup</a>, which was first run in 2004. </p>
      <p>Athletes from Moldova have won European medals in <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">Athletics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biathlon" title="Biathlon">Biathlon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">Gymnastics</a>, World medals in <a href="/wiki/Archery" title="Archery">Archery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">Judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">Swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">Taekwondo</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> medals in <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">Boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canoeing" title="Canoeing">Canoeing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shooting" title="Shooting">Shooting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">Weightlifting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">Wrestling</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moldova&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>
      <div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-fn1-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-fn1_38-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Jewish minority was more numerous in the past (228,620 Jews in Bessarabia in 1897, or 11.8% of the population).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-fn2-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-fn2_55-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Note:</i> Further 11,844 were deported on 12–13 June 1941 from other Romanian territories occupied by the USSR a year earlier.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-fn6-198"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-fn6_198-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Prince <a href="/wiki/Dimitrie_Cantemir" title="Dimitrie Cantemir">Dimitrie Cantemir</a> was one of the most important figures of Moldavian culture of the 18th century. He wrote the first geographical, ethnographic and economic description of the country. <span class="languageicon">(in Latin)</span> <i><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/la:Descriptio_Moldaviae" class="extiw" title="s:la:Descriptio Moldaviae">Descriptio Moldaviae</a></i>, (Berlin, 1714), at Latin Wikisource.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>

           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFCharles_Upson_Clark1927" class="citation web cs1">Charles Upson Clark (1927). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://depts.washington.edu/cartah/text_archive/clark/bc_8.shtml#bc_8">"Bessarabia, Chapter VIII: Russia Organizes the Province"</a>. <i>Depts.washington.edu</i>. Dodd, Mead &amp; Company<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">9 October</span> 2013</span>. <q>Today, the Bulgarians form one of the most solid elements in Southern Bessarabia, numbering (with the Gagauzes, i.e., Turkish-speaking Christians also from the Dobrudja) nearly 150,000. Colonization brought in numerous Great Russian peasants, and the Russian bureaucracy imported Russian office-holders and professional men; according to the Romanian estimate of 1920, there were about 75,000 (2.9%) Great Russians in the territory, and the Lipovans and Cossacks numbered 59,000 (2.2%); the Little Russians (Ukrainians) came to 254,000 (9.6%). That, plus about 10,000 Poles, brings the total number of Slavs to 545,000 in a population of 2,631,000, or about one-fifth.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Depts.washington.edu&amp;rft.atitle=Bessarabia%2C+Chapter+VIII%3A+Russia+Organizes+the+Province&amp;rft.date=1927&amp;rft.au=Charles+Upson+Clark&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fdepts.washington.edu%2Fcartah%2Ftext_archive%2Fclark%2Fbc_8.shtml%23bc_8&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMoldova" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>

ammari%2C+Khalaf+F.&amp;rft.au=Saleem%2C+Muhammad&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC5451287&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMoldova"
